2:11:276:30:30:118:496:651:14:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:Property and Contract Rights in Autocracies and Democracies

3:41:1304:0:27:283:331:675:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:Abstract 
3:42:1312:27:28:72:75:648:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman: 
3:43:1312:28:27:72:75:620:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman: 
3:44:1312:27:28:108:510:593:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:We present and test empirically a new theory of property and contract rights.    Any 
3:45:1397:28:27:72:543:565:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:incentive an autocrat has to respect such rights comes from his interest in future tax collections and 
3:46:1500:27:28:72:517:538:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:national income and increases with his planning horizon.    We find    a compelling empirical 
3:47:1594:28:28:72:542:510:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:relationship between property and contract rights and an autocrat's time in power.    In lasting -- but 
3:48:1697:28:27:72:532:482:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:not in new -- democracies, the same rule of law and individual rights that ensure continued free 
3:49:1793:27:28:72:524:455:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:elections entail extensive property and contract rights.    We show that the age of a democratic 
3:50:1890:28:27:72:375:427:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:system is strongly correlated with property and contract rights. 
3:51:1954:27:28:72:75:400:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman: 
3:52:1954:28:28:72:75:372:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman: 
3:53:1954:28:0:72:141:344:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:JEL O00, 010 
4:54:1967:0:27:72:152:675:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:1. Introduction 
4:55:1982:27:28:108:543:648:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:What types of governments are most likely to have economic policies and institutions that 
4:56:2071:28:27:72:530:620:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:generate good economic performance?    There are examples of good -- and of bad -- economic 
4:57:2161:27:28:72:533:593:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:performance under both autocratic and democratic governments.    Many empirical studies have 
4:58:2254:28:27:72:529:565:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:compared the economic performance of autocracies and democracies, but their conclusions are 
4:59:2346:27:28:72:532:538:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:remarkably varied and inconclusive.    We shall show here that it is naive to suppose that one of 
4:60:2444:28:28:72:533:510:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:these types of political systems will regularly have better economic performance than the other. 
4:61:2540:28:27:108:523:482:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:The quality of economic policies and institutions depends partly on the incentives and 
4:62:2627:27:28:72:528:455:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:constraints that face those who make governmental and legal decisions.    These incentives and 
4:63:2722:28:27:72:543:427:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:constraints vary from one autocracy to another and from one democracy to another.    We contend 
4:64:2818:27:28:72:519:400:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:that they vary so much within these two types of regimes that any empirical tests that merely 
4:65:2912:28:28:72:527:372:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:distinguish governments as autocratic or democratic are bound to be mis-specified.    We show 
4:66:3006:28:27:72:543:344:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:that, when appropriate distinctions are drawn within each of these two types of governments, clear 
4:67:3105:27:28:72:257:317:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:and robust empirical findings emerge. 
4:68:3142:28:27:108:543:289:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:The importance of incentives within different types of governments becomes immediately 
4:69:3229:27:28:72:532:262:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:evident when we think about the sometimes hoped-for benevolent dictator who understands (or 
4:70:3321:28:28:72:531:234:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:who is guided by economic advisers who understand) the advantages of markets and uses them 
4:71:3412:28:27:72:545:206:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:effectively to elicit economic growth through the rational self-interested behavior of his subjects.   
4:72:3515:27:28:72:511:179:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:A moment's reflection reveals a methodological inconsistency: if the autocrat's subjects are 
4:73:3608:28:28:72:530:151:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:supposed to be self-interested, we should impartially assume that the autocrat will also take his 
4:74:3706:28:27:72:519:123:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:own interests into account.    If he does, then whenever insecurity about his hold on power or 
4:75:3801:27:0:72:525:96:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:anything else gives him a short time horizon, he will gain from expropriating any assets of his 
5:76:3898:0:27:72:531:675:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:subjects whose tax-yield to him over the short time horizon is less than their capital value.    He 
5:77:3998:27:28:72:543:648:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:will typically also gain resources by printing money to spend on his own purposes, thereby taxing 
5:78:4096:28:27:72:542:620:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:real money balances through inflation, and by repudiating his debts.    Such measures increase the 
5:79:4195:27:28:72:536:593:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:resources he can use to attempt to keep himself in power or to serve his interests in other ways.   
5:80:4295:28:27:72:541:565:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:There are countless examples throughout history of autocrats who have taken such measures.    In 
5:81:4392:27:28:72:537:538:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:such cases, the rational self-interest of an autocrat is inconsistent with the private property rights 
5:82:4495:28:28:72:322:510:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:that are necessary for an effective market economy. 
5:83:4546:28:27:108:528:482:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:By contrast, a similarly rational and self-interested autocrat expecting to rule for a long 
5:84:4638:27:28:72:518:455:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:time (and especially one with dynastic expectations) would gain from respecting -- and even 
5:85:4729:28:27:72:543:427:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:protecting -- the property of his subjects.    This would increase investment and future productivity 
5:86:4830:27:28:72:537:400:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:and thus also his long-run tax collections.    There are also many historical examples of autocrats 
5:87:4930:28:28:72:326:372:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:who have served their long-run interests in this way. 
5:88:4983:28:27:108:534:344:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:Thus autocrats with different time horizons face dramatically different incentives.    This 
5:89:5075:27:28:72:509:317:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:means that we cannot correctly estimate the impact of autocratic government on economic 
5:90:5162:28:27:72:516:289:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:performance without taking the time horizons of the individual autocrats into account.    The 
5:91:5256:27:28:72:451:262:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:empirical results in this paper suggest that this is a matter of some importance. 
5:92:5337:28:28:108:525:234:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:Consider now the factors that can endanger property and contract rights in a beginning 
5:93:5423:28:27:72:524:206:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:democracy.    Suppose the democratic debut involves nothing more than an election that gives 
5:94:5516:27:28:72:534:179:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:victory to some political leader or optimizing party.    When an elected leader has such power, it 
5:95:5615:28:28:72:540:151:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:brings him benefits, so we cannot take it for granted that democratic leaders will be indifferent to 
5:96:5716:28:27:72:543:123:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:whether or not they continue in power or that they will exercise their power without regard to their 
5:97:5817:27:0:72:539:96:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:own interests.    The elected leadership might maximize its chances of re-election by confiscating 
6:98:5917:0:27:72:534:675:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:the assets of unpopular minorities or of the rich and distributing the proceeds among those from 
6:99:6014:27:28:72:522:648:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:whom it hopes to obtain a majority in the next election.    It might sometimes also improve its 
6:100:6110:28:27:72:543:620:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:chances of staying in power by seizing opposing media of communication, or the assets of political 
6:101:6209:27:28:72:397:593:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:opponents, or any firms or fortunes that are linked to its opponents. 
6:102:6278:28:27:108:540:565:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:Such measures terminate or at least endanger the democracy (and often are a sign that the 
6:103:6368:27:28:72:543:538:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:current elected leader is on the way to becoming a dictator).    They could not even be implemented 
6:104:6468:28:28:72:508:510:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:if the democracy has courts that rigorously enforce the rule of law.    But an initial election 
6:105:6564:28:27:72:543:482:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:(however fair) does not by itself guarantee that there is an effective legal system enforcing the rule 
6:106:6667:27:28:72:526:455:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:of law.    Thus transitory democracies can easily suffer from expropriations that have the same 
6:107:6763:28:27:72:543:427:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:harmful effects on property rights as the predations of an autocrat.    If a government does not have 
6:108:6865:27:28:72:527:400:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:(or respect) the legal mechanisms that constrain usurpations of individual rights, it cannot be a 
6:109:6963:28:28:72:355:372:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:lasting democracy, but some democracies do not last long. 
6:110:7020:28:27:108:493:344:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:The situation in a lasting democracy is utterly different not only from transitory 
6:111:7103:27:28:72:522:317:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:democracies but also from autocratic governments.    Though lasting democracies suffer from 
6:112:7195:28:27:72:542:289:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:sclerotic accumulations of special-interest lobbying and (like all other types of governments) often 
6:113:7296:27:28:72:499:262:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:have economically inefficient policies, they necessarily hold elections under law and the 
6:114:7385:28:28:72:539:234:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:governmental leaders or parties that are defeated surrender power in accord with the law.    There 
6:115:7484:28:27:72:542:206:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:cannot be genuine elections unless even the leading opponents of the party in power have not only 
6:116:7581:27:28:72:541:179:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:political rights but also the economic rights needed to obtain a livelihood.    If even those who are 
6:117:7683:28:28:72:543:151:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:the main competitors of the existing leaders of government have these rights, they should normally 
6:118:7782:28:27:72:537:123:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:be available to others as well.    (This is true of any lasting representative government, whether it 
6:119:7884:27:0:72:526:96:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:has universal adult suffrage, such as is typical now, or a more restrictive suffrage, such as was 
7:120:7983:0:27:72:518:675:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:characteristic of representative governments in the nineteenth century and earlier.    Thus our 
7:121:8079:27:28:72:534:648:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:argument applies to all representative governments, but since the representative governments in 
7:122:8175:28:27:72:515:620:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:our data base are overwhelmingly universal suffrage democracies, we use the familiar word 
7:123:8265:27:28:72:336:593:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:"democracy" to cover all representative governments.) 
7:124:8318:28:27:108:525:565:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:Moreover, the independent judiciary, the courts, the respect for law, or whatever other 
7:125:8406:27:28:72:517:538:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:mechanisms ensure that a democracy abides by competitive elections held according to law, 
7:126:8496:28:28:72:530:510:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:necessarily also ensure that the citizenry has the freedom to do whatever is permitted under the 
7:127:8593:28:27:72:532:482:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:law.    This freedom by definition provides some individual rights: individuals have the socially 
7:128:8691:27:28:72:543:455:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:protected right to do whatever is not prohibited by law.    Property rights are simply the individual 
7:129:8792:28:27:72:542:427:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:rights that relate to things that may be bought and sold.    As James Madison put it, just "as a man is 
7:130:8896:27:28:72:523:400:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:said to have a right to his property, he may equally be said to have a property in his rights."1  
7:131:8994:28:28:72:527:372:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:Property and contract rights are protected by the same institutions that protect other individual 
7:132:9092:28:27:72:516:344:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:rights.    Societies are therefore constrained in their choices: they cannot prohibit all types of 
7:133:9191:27:28:72:542:317:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:private property and freedom of contract and also have a lasting democracy.    A stable democracy 
7:134:9288:28:27:72:517:289:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:without any property and contract rights is not in the feasible set.    All lasting representative 
7:135:9387:27:28:72:531:262:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:governments that have been observed, however wise or unwise their laws may be, always have 
7:136:9478:28:133:72:259:234:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:extensive property and contract rights. 
7:137:9517:133:11:72:221:101:12:g_d0_f8:12:g_d0_f8:                               
7:138:9547:11:0:108:395:90:6:Times New Roman:10:Times New Roman:1  In the National Gazette for March 27, 1792 (Madison Papers, 1983). 
8:139:9616:0:27:108:537:675:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:Whereas in an autocracy it is the leader's interest in his future tax returns (and thus in the 
8:140:9711:27:28:72:539:648:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:future income of his domain) that is the source of any property and contract rights, in any lasting 
8:141:9811:28:27:72:541:620:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:democracy it is the very mechanisms that ensure that a leader can not unilaterally extend his hold 
8:142:9908:27:28:72:532:593:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:on power that are the source of property and contract rights.    Though some democracies suffer 
8:143:10004:28:27:72:541:565:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:from excessive turnover of leadership, the legal replacement of democratic leaders is in general a 
8:144:10103:27:28:72:517:538:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:sign of the effective rule of law, and thus of the property and contract rights of the citizenry. 
8:145:10199:28:28:108:543:510:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:Property and contract rights in a democracy rest mainly on the need, if the democracy is to 
8:146:10291:28:27:72:546:482:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:last, to leave decisions about whether the law is being followed to relatively disinterested parties.   
8:147:10394:27:28:72:526:455:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:Political leaders have an incentive to interpret the law in whatever way best furthers their own 
8:148:10491:28:27:72:543:427:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:interests, so a democracy will not last if they can interpret the law as they please.    The rule of law 
8:149:10596:27:28:72:539:400:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:needed for a lasting democracy will prevail only if disputes under the law are adjudicated mainly 
8:150:10693:28:28:72:539:372:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:by individuals who have no stake in the dispute.    This in turn requires institutions that, by social 
8:151:10796:28:27:72:538:344:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:design, have a very special structure of incentives and constraints: one in which those who make 
8:152:10892:27:28:72:543:317:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:decisions do not share in the losses or gains of any party to the dispute, and in which a knowledge 
8:153:10992:28:27:72:506:289:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:of the law and a reputation for fairness increases the chances for advancement.    To last, a 
8:154:11086:27:28:72:518:262:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:democracy must maintain and abide by such institutions, notably courts with an independent 
8:155:11177:28:28:72:120:234:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:judiciary. 
8:156:11187:28:27:108:532:206:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:We hypothesize that the dependence of any lasting democracy on legal institutions with 
8:157:11274:27:28:72:522:179:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:this special structure of incentives and constraints is the main source of property and contract 
8:158:11371:28:28:72:543:151:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:rights in democracies.   In an autocracy, on the other hand, the autocrat is by definition the source 
8:159:11473:28:27:72:506:123:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:of law and thus above the law and able to override any of his courts.    Thus his motive for 
8:160:11566:27:0:72:537:96:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:providing property and contract rights, even if they are provided through courts, is rather mainly 
9:161:11666:0:27:72:531:675:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:his interest in the income and taxable capacity of his domain.    The structures of incentives and 
9:162:11765:27:28:72:513:648:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:constraints that give rise to property and contract rights in democracies and autocracies are, 
9:163:11860:28:27:72:231:620:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:therefore, dramatically different. 
9:164:11894:27:28:108:542:593:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:The foregoing logic leads us to hypothesize that in autocracies it is the time horizon of the 
9:165:11988:28:27:72:543:565:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:individual autocrat (or, occasionally, the ruling clique) that is the main determinant of property and 
9:166:12090:27:28:72:542:538:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:contract rights, whereas in democracies these rights depend upon whether the democratic system is 
9:167:12187:28:28:72:114:510:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:durable. 
9:168:12195:28:27:108:543:482:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:Many democracies are transitory and such property and contract rights as they provide can 
9:169:12285:27:28:72:518:455:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:be quite inferior to those provided by some secure autocrats.    An autocrat has, however, the 
9:170:12380:28:27:72:500:427:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:capacity to seize any assets in the country that he rules, whereas no single individual in a 
9:171:12473:27:28:72:523:400:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:continuing democracy can unilaterally seize the assets of others or abrogate their rights under 
9:172:12569:28:28:72:543:372:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:contracts.    Any autocratic society will sooner or later come to have rulers with short time horizons 
9:173:12672:28:27:72:530:344:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:due to succession crises or other causes.    We therefore hypothesize that democracies that have 
9:174:12769:27:28:72:527:317:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:lasted for some time and are expected to last much longer provide better property and contract 
9:175:12864:28:27:72:539:289:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:rights than any other type of regime.    The societies that are consistently havens for capital flight 
9:176:12966:27:28:72:495:262:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:and that have experienced steady capital accumulation across generations are all lasting 
9:177:13055:28:28:72:141:234:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:democracies.2 
9:178:13068:28:27:108:541:206:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:In this paper we test empirically the theory that has just been described.    Section 2 shows 
9:179:13162:27:28:72:527:179:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:how the theory lends itself to relatively straightforward empirical tests, both because here past 
9:180:13260:28:28:72:534:151:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:experience is a relatively good guide to the future, and also because the tests are not likely to be 
9:181:13361:28:22:72:543:123:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:subject to any severe endogeneity problems.    Section 3 describes our data on regime type, regime 
9:182:13460:22:11:72:221:101:12:g_d0_f8:12:g_d0_f8:                               
9:183:13490:11:0:108:520:90:6:Times New Roman:10:Times New Roman:2  The foregoing theory is set out more fully in Olson (1991, 1993) and in McGuire and Olson (1996). 
10:184:13591:0:27:72:542:675:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:duration, and property rights.    Section 4 reports empirical findings on property rights and regime 
10:185:13692:27:28:72:542:648:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:type, while Section 5 presents findings on property rights and regime duration.    Sections 6, 7, and 
10:186:13793:28:27:72:521:620:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:8 test the robustness of our results and show that they are not an artifact of reverse causation, 
10:187:13891:27:28:72:507:593:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:sample selection, measurement error, or heteroskedasticity.    We conclude with Section 9. 
10:188:13980:28:27:72:202:565:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:2. Empirical Tractability 
10:189:14005:27:28:108:543:538:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:However long a political regime has survived, the incentive structure changes drastically if 
10:190:14098:28:28:72:535:510:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:that regime is expected to collapse soon.    This expectation will not only change behavior in the 
10:191:14197:28:27:72:542:482:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:political system, but will also alter behavior in the market.    Even if property or contract rights are 
10:192:14302:27:28:72:522:455:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:good at the moment, it will usually not pay to make long-term contracts or investments if one 
10:193:14396:28:27:72:502:427:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:expects that contracts will not be enforced or property rights protected a year from now.   
10:194:14488:27:28:72:540:400:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:Therefore, the institutions and policies that determine contract and property rights, like monetary 
10:195:14588:28:28:72:536:372:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:and macroeconomic policies, affect reality not only directly but also through their impact on the 
10:196:14686:28:27:72:304:344:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:expectations of the participants in the economy. 
10:197:14734:27:28:108:530:317:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:It might seem that, because expectations about the future are important, yet not directly 
10:198:14824:28:27:72:543:289:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:measurable, the foregoing theory would be difficult to test.    In fact, there are some important and 
10:199:14926:27:28:72:543:262:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:interesting reasons that make empirical testing relatively straightforward.    The idea that the past is 
10:200:15031:28:28:72:280:234:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:prologue is especially relevant in this area. 
10:201:15076:28:27:108:512:206:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:Consider democratic systems first.    The length of time that a legal system has been 
10:202:15162:27:28:72:503:179:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:operating is a major determinant of how well property and contract rights are defined and 
10:203:15251:28:28:72:533:151:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:delineated.    It is beyond the wit of man to think of all possible contingencies that might lead to 
10:204:15352:28:27:72:533:123:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:disputes about contracts or property.    Thus legal systems that have litigated a great many cases 
10:205:15451:27:0:72:535:96:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:and have accumulated a vast store of precedents offer better defined and delineated contract and 
11:206:15549:0:27:72:543:675:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:property rights than otherwise similar systems that have just started.    Some new political systems 
11:207:15650:27:28:72:543:648:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:have dealt with this problem by adopting wholesale the commercial codes and court precedents of 
11:208:15746:28:27:72:524:620:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:other countries.    Though in some cases, such as in the continued use of English common law 
11:209:15839:27:28:72:527:593:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:precedents in the United States after it achieved independence, this is relatively easy, there are 
11:210:15938:28:27:72:506:565:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:often substantial problems arising from differences in technology, customs, language, and 
11:211:16027:27:28:72:539:538:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:experience between the country with the new political system and the country whose legal codes 
11:212:16122:28:28:72:523:510:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:and precedents are being adopted.    Thus the length of time a legal system has been operating 
11:213:16217:28:27:72:463:482:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:affects the way it works, quite apart from the way that its age affects its viability. 
11:214:16303:27:28:108:516:455:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:The impact of age on viability is nicely illustrated by elections in the United States.   
11:215:16393:28:27:72:532:427:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:Though there are substantial industries that do economic and political forecasting, one virtually 
11:216:16491:27:28:72:524:400:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:never sees forecasts about whether, say, the 1998 Congressional elections will take place.    In 
11:217:16587:28:28:72:536:372:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:large part because elections in the US have been held as scheduled for more than 200 years, it is 
11:218:16685:28:27:72:534:344:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:simply taken for granted that they will be held as scheduled.    Similarly, the fact that the British 
11:219:16787:27:28:72:532:317:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:court system has protected property and contract rights with continuity for more than 300 years 
11:220:16883:28:27:72:543:289:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:means that certain property and contract rights in Britain are not the object of explicit forecasts, but 
11:221:16988:27:28:72:536:262:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:are unthinkingly taken for granted.    Such tacit assumptions about the institutional reality are, in 
11:222:17090:28:28:72:542:234:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:turn, part of the institutional reality: what everyone expects -- and especially what everyone takes 
11:223:17190:28:27:72:527:206:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:for granted -- is more likely to happen precisely because of these explicit or tacit expectations. 
11:224:17287:27:28:108:543:179:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:New democracies not only usually lack the security that comes from such expectations, but 
11:225:17377:28:28:72:542:151:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:they are often also set up in extremely fluid -- and sometimes nearly anarchic -- situations.    When 
11:226:17477:28:27:72:540:123:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:the flag of a new democracy is raised, it may not even be clear how many will salute: there is not 
11:227:17576:27:0:72:535:96:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:only uncertainty about how long the new democracy will last, but sometimes it is not even clear 
12:228:17674:0:27:72:483:675:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:that the new democracy has the power needed to protect property and contract rights. 
12:229:17758:27:28:108:543:648:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:Thus we conclude that the age of a democratic political system is not only directly pertinent 
12:230:17852:28:27:72:543:620:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:to the property and contract rights in a democracy, but also a reasonable proxy measure of both the 
12:231:17952:27:28:72:533:593:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:likelihood and the popular expectation that a given democratic system and the rights it provides 
12:232:18049:28:27:72:240:565:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:will last for the foreseeable future. 
12:233:18086:27:28:108:532:538:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:Now let us consider autocracy.    It is instructive to start with Mao's maxim that political 
12:234:18179:28:28:72:538:510:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:power grows out of the barrel of a gun.    Accepting this maxim does not imply, however, that an 
12:235:18276:28:27:72:542:482:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:autocrat is the best marksman in the country, much less that he personally could outgun any large 
12:236:18374:27:28:72:535:455:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:number of his subjects.    The power of an autocrat when he is powerful grows mainly out of the 
12:237:18470:28:27:72:525:427:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:belief that his subordinates will use their guns in the service of the autocrat, thereby making it 
12:238:18569:27:28:72:543:400:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:exceedingly costly for other subjects to rebel.    But who guards the guards?    What explains why a 
12:239:18670:28:28:72:543:372:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:given officer in the autocrat's army or police will obey the autocrat's orders, when they do, in fact, 
12:240:18773:28:27:72:534:344:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:obey?    If any officer expects that all or almost all of the other officers will follow the autocrat's 
12:241:18876:27:28:72:543:317:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:orders, then he has no choice but to follow these orders also.    What each of the other officers does 
12:242:18979:28:27:72:543:289:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:also depends on what they, in turn, expect their colleagues to do.    If almost everyone expects that 
12:243:19080:27:28:72:533:262:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:almost all of the officers will follow the autocrat's orders, the autocrat is securely in control and 
12:244:19182:28:28:72:520:234:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:likely to remain in control for some time.    What it is rational to do depends on what average 
12:245:19278:28:27:72:542:206:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:opinion expects average opinion to be.    When someone has appointed himself the new autocrat, it 
12:246:19376:27:28:72:531:179:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:is usually not clear what each officer will expect, or expect that his colleagues will expect.    So 
12:247:19477:28:28:72:527:151:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:autocrats who have not consolidated their power do not, in fact, necessarily have much power. 
12:248:19570:28:27:108:542:123:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:Thus the power of an autocrat is in large part the outcome of a coordination game.    Just as 
12:249:19664:27:0:72:532:96:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:it is irrational to drive on a different side of the road than other people going the same direction 
13:250:19767:0:27:72:548:675:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:expect to use, so it is irrational to ignore the expectations of others in assessing an autocrat's power.   
13:251:19875:27:28:72:543:648:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:This means that usually the longer that an autocrat exercises power,    the more people will take for 
13:252:19977:28:27:72:401:620:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:granted that his orders will be followed, and the more power he has. 
13:253:20045:27:28:108:543:593:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:One check on the validity of the foregoing arguments is the correlation between the elapsed 
13:254:20136:28:27:72:543:565:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:duration of an autocrat's rule and the likelihood of a coup.    We calculated the probability of a coup 
13:255:20240:27:28:72:542:538:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:for all regimes for all years from the data for 1948-82 as a ratio of two numbers.    The numerator is 
13:256:20343:28:28:72:541:510:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:the sum of all autocrats who were deposed by a coup in year t of their tenure. The denominator is 
13:257:20440:28:27:72:512:482:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:the sum of all autocrats with tenure greater than or equal to t - 1.    The probabilities of both 
13:258:20536:27:28:72:526:455:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:successful and unsuccessful coup attempts are quite high in the first five years of an autocrat's 
13:259:20634:28:27:72:533:427:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:tenure, but decline dramatically as duration increases.    The probability of a coup attempt in the 
13:260:20734:27:28:72:534:400:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:first year (including successful coups) is 32%, 20% in the second year, and below 10% for most 
13:261:20829:28:28:72:543:372:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:years beyond the sixth.    This pattern suggests that the duration of an autocrat's rule is a reasonable 
13:262:20934:28:27:72:500:344:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:approximation of regime stability and expected remaining duration.    This pattern is also 
13:263:21025:27:28:72:543:317:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:consistent with our use of the log of duration in all empirical specifications, so that increases from, 
13:264:21129:28:27:72:543:289:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:say, 0 to 3 years in the elapsed duration of an autocrat's rule are weighted much more heavily than 
13:265:21229:27:28:72:522:262:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:increases from 10 to 13 years.    A similar calculation was made for democracies.    Again, the 
13:266:21325:28:28:72:515:234:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:probabilities of successful and unsuccessful coups tend to decline as the elapsed duration of 
13:267:21419:28:27:72:259:206:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:democracy within a country increases. 
13:268:21456:27:28:108:541:179:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:It might be thought that the expected remaining duration of an autocrat's regime would be 
13:269:21546:28:28:72:543:151:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:inversely related to the age of the autocrat, since human life is finite and this sets a maximum value 
13:270:21649:28:27:72:540:123:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:on the expected remaining duration of an autocrat's regime.    Age and duration increase together, 
13:271:21748:27:0:72:543:96:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:making duration to date a suspect proxy for the expected remaining time in power.    However, the 
14:272:21848:0:27:72:543:675:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:prospects of natural death constrain the time horizons of even very old leaders less than one might 
14:273:21948:27:28:72:516:648:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:expect.    The probability of death from natural causes in a particular year is not high even at 
14:274:22045:28:27:72:543:620:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:advanced ages.    From the life tables of the United States, average remaining years of life exceeds 
14:275:22146:27:28:72:543:593:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:five years even for an 80-year-old male.    Furthermore, our use of the log of duration ensures that 
14:276:22247:28:27:72:543:565:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:minimal weight is given to further increases in tenure for aging autocrats of long standing included 
14:277:22348:27:28:72:531:538:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:in our sample, such as Banda of Malawi and Franco of Spain.    In any event, the expectation of 
14:278:22444:28:28:72:542:510:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:natural death will have less impact on an autocrat's incentives than the expectation of exiting via a 
14:279:22546:28:27:72:543:482:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:coup.    An autocrat may spend substantial amounts of a country's resources attempting to stave off 
14:280:22646:27:28:72:541:455:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:a coup -- or preparing for a luxurious exile -- but there are limits to what he can usefully spend to 
14:281:22746:28:27:72:542:427:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:stave off natural death.    A proxy measure that declined in value when autocrats reached advanced 
14:282:22845:27:28:72:529:400:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:ages thus might be a less accurate measure of incentives to protect property rights than the one 
14:283:22942:28:28:72:123:372:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:used here. 
14:284:22952:28:27:108:533:344:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:Thus we take the elapsed duration of an autocrat's (or an autocratic group's) rule and the 
14:285:23043:27:28:72:543:317:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:current age of a democratic system as proxies for its expected remaining life: what has survived for 
14:286:23144:28:27:72:539:289:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:a long time is expected to be more likely to last than that which is new.    In summary, our theory 
14:287:23244:27:28:72:518:262:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:leads us to predict a positive relationship, for both autocracies and democracies, between the 
14:288:23339:28:28:72:543:234:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:duration of a regime and the security of the property and contract rights that its citizens enjoy.    For 
14:289:23445:28:27:72:532:206:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:both types of regimes, this positive relationship is the result of the joint hypotheses that (1) past 
14:290:23547:27:28:72:529:179:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:duration of the regime is positively related to expected future duration, and (2) expected future 
14:291:23645:28:28:72:517:151:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:duration is positively related to the security of property and contract rights.    In addition, for 
14:292:23745:28:27:72:538:123:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:democracies we argue (3) that the mechanisms that support contract and property rights function 
14:293:23841:27:0:72:516:96:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:better, the longer the democracy has been continuously in existence, apart from the effect of 
15:294:23937:0:27:72:518:675:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:duration on expectations of its future life.    Though the incentive structures underlying these 
15:295:24033:27:28:72:530:648:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:relationships are different for democracies and autocracies, the expected empirical relationship 
15:296:24130:28:27:72:311:620:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:between duration and property rights is the same. 
15:297:24179:27:28:108:535:593:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:There is another reason why testing the implications of the foregoing theory is relatively 
15:298:24270:28:27:72:542:565:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:straightforward.    The key causal variables are the age of a democratic system and the duration of 
15:299:24369:27:28:72:534:538:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:an individual autocrat's rule.    As Grossman and Noh (1990) have shown, the time in office of a 
15:300:24465:28:28:72:542:510:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:democratic leader in a political system with free entry is likely to be quite sensitive to the policies 
15:301:24569:28:27:72:543:482:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:chosen by that leader.    A leader or political party with a rapacious policy is much less likely to be 
15:302:24673:27:28:72:533:455:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:able to win support for continuation in office than one that has followed a policy that favors the 
15:303:24772:28:27:72:505:427:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:welfare of the citizenry.  To determine the relationship between the tenure in office of an 
15:304:24864:27:28:72:530:400:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:individual democratic leader and his impact on property and contract rights, one would have to 
15:305:24959:28:28:72:543:372:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:measure not only the effect of leaders' time horizons on the policies they chose, but also the impact 
15:306:25060:28:27:72:542:344:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:of the policies chosen on the probability of re-election.    There would presumably be strong causal 
15:307:25161:27:28:72:533:317:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:connections going in both directions and this would complicate empirical testing.    By contrast, 
15:308:25259:28:27:72:527:289:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:when the age of a democratic system -- or the length of a single autocrat's rule -- is at issue the 
15:309:25354:27:28:72:255:262:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:situation is relatively straightforward. 
15:310:25394:28:28:108:543:234:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:In a secure democracy in which the continuation of representative government is taken for 
15:311:25484:28:27:72:542:206:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:granted, the incumbent leader may not even give any thought to the implications of his policies for 
15:312:25584:27:28:72:543:179:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:the life of the political system.    The property and contract rights at issue are, moreover, more often 
15:313:25689:28:28:72:543:151:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:the province of the courts and the legal system than of the elected officials.    In a democracy that is 
15:314:25794:28:27:72:532:123:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:quite insecure the courts may be much weaker and the incumbent leader obviously may take an 
15:315:25885:27:0:72:532:96:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:interest in the question of how long the democracy will last, since his position as leader may be 
16:316:25985:0:27:72:513:675:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:affected.    But it would be wrong to conclude that he is necessarily motivated by a desire to 
16:317:26079:27:28:72:539:648:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:prolong the life of the democracy: he could, for the reasons set out above, also be motivated by a 
16:318:26178:28:27:72:542:620:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:desire to become a dictator who does not have to continue to answer to the electorate.    Thus, just 
16:319:26279:27:28:72:528:593:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:as he might choose policies that are intended to increase the life of the democracy, so he might 
16:320:26375:28:27:72:543:565:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:choose policies with the opposite objective.    While our theoretical framework suggests that there 
16:321:26475:27:28:72:543:538:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:should be a strong tendency for lasting democracies to have better individual rights than those that 
16:322:26576:28:28:72:524:510:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:have not yet been securely established, it does not suggest that there should be any strong and 
16:323:26672:28:27:72:541:482:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:regular tendency for democratic leaders to choose policies about property and contract rights that 
16:324:26771:27:28:72:534:455:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:are intended to change the duration of the democratic system.    Accordingly, our theory implies 
16:325:26868:28:27:72:536:427:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:that the age of a democratic system is not directly influenced by policy choices.    Policy choices 
16:326:26968:27:28:72:538:400:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:may influence the survival probability of a democratic system through their impact on economic 
16:327:27063:28:28:72:533:372:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:performance, but we control for per capita GDP levels and growth rates and this should capture 
16:328:27158:28:27:72:514:344:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:much of the effect of any endogenous policy choices.    We shall later see that our statistical 
16:329:27254:27:28:72:323:317:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:examination of this issue offers further reassurance. 
16:330:27307:28:27:108:540:289:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:In the case of autocracy, there can be no doubt that an autocrat has an incentive to choose 
16:331:27399:27:28:72:543:262:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:policies that will extend his tenure.    Though this effect can indeed lead to bias in our estimates, the 
16:332:27505:28:28:72:534:234:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:bias runs against our hypothesis.    We assume autocrats optimize, so that an autocrat with a low 
16:333:27603:28:27:72:481:206:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:survival probability increases his exactions and reduces his expenditures on the legal 
16:334:27689:27:28:72:517:179:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:infrastructure.    One reason he does this is because he has little reason to take account of the 
16:335:27787:28:28:72:542:151:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:reduction in future tax receipts that this brings about.    Another reason is that he rationally gives a 
16:336:27892:28:27:72:516:123:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:relatively higher value to resources that he can obtain now to shore up his hold on power by 
16:337:27985:27:0:72:513:96:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:strengthening his instruments of social control and by subsidizing pivotal allies.    Though a 
17:338:28082:0:27:72:524:675:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:government whose survival depends on popularity with an electorate may gain from lowering 
17:339:28172:27:28:72:541:648:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:taxes, an autocrat's tenure does not depend on any electorate.    It typically depends instead on the 
17:340:28274:28:27:72:528:620:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:power and loyalty of his military and police forces and on the support of his allies.3  He needs 
17:341:28371:27:28:72:543:593:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:resources to obtain this power, loyalty, and support.    If most autocrats tried to extend their tenures 
17:342:28476:28:27:72:543:565:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:by improving the welfare of their subjects, much of the effects of this behavior would in any event 
17:343:28576:27:28:72:445:538:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:be captured by per capita GDP levels and growth rates, which we control for. 
17:344:28652:28:28:108:526:510:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:Thus in our model an autocrat's incentive to increase taxes and reduce expenditures on 
17:345:28739:28:27:72:528:482:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:legal infrastructure improves his survival probabilities.    Higher taxes still have an opportunity 
17:346:28838:27:28:72:521:455:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:cost for an autocrat, however: higher taxes (and insecure property and contract rights) reduce 
17:347:28933:28:27:72:542:427:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:future GDP levels.    At a sufficiently high probability of survival, the costs of foregone future tax 
17:348:29036:27:28:72:542:400:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:revenues from reducing GDP outstrip the benefits from using current tax revenues to extend one's 
17:349:29133:28:28:72:543:372:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:tenure, particularly if one makes the reasonable assumption that survival probabilities increase at a 
17:350:29235:28:197:72:459:344:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:diminishing rate as expenditures on repressive forces and pivotal allies increase. 
17:351:29317:197:11:72:221:147:12:g_d0_f8:12:g_d0_f8:                               
17:352:29347:11:16:108:540:136:6:Times New Roman:10:Times New Roman:3  See Olson (1965) on the logic behind this conclusion and Lichbach (1995) for a most thorough survey of 
17:353:29453:16:11:72:529:120:10:Times New Roman:10:Times New Roman:the literature on this subject.    See also Svensson (1994) for a broadly similar model in which investments in legal 
17:354:29571:11:12:72:542:109:10:Times New Roman:10:Times New Roman:infrastructure in period 1 are negatively related to the current government's prospects of remaining in power in period 
17:355:29691:12:11:72:530:97:10:Times New Roman:10:Times New Roman:2.    Unlike our results reported below, Svensson's empirical tests utilize only country-level averages of instability, 
17:356:29811:11:0:72:421:86:10:Times New Roman:10:Times New Roman:property rights, and investment, and do not differentiate democracies from autocracies. 
18:357:29899:0:27:108:530:675:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:Accordingly, optimization by insecure autocrats assures that they adjust their economic 
18:358:29986:27:28:72:533:648:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:policies to make their tenure less short or insecure than it would otherwise be.    They do this by 
18:359:30086:28:27:72:531:620:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:increasing their exactions or confiscations to obtain more resources for protecting their hold on 
18:360:30184:27:28:72:501:593:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:power.    To the extent that autocrats who would otherwise have a short tenure succeed in 
18:361:30274:28:27:72:519:565:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:extending their hold on power, our coefficients on the duration of autocrats tend to be biased 
18:362:30369:27:28:72:542:538:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:downward: those insecure autocrats whose expedient expropriations have enabled them to cling to 
18:363:30465:28:28:72:543:510:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:power for extended periods reduce the generally positive association between the elapsed duration 
18:364:30563:28:27:72:541:482:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:of an autocrat's rule and the security of property and contract rights.    We nonetheless later report 
18:365:30666:27:28:72:543:455:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:the results of tests that correct for the possibility our coefficients are biased upwards by a feedback 
18:366:30770:28:27:72:291:427:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:from improved policies to lengthened tenure. 
18:367:30814:27:28:72:75:400:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman: 
18:368:30814:28:28:72:415:372:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:3. Regime Types, Regime Duration and Property Rights: The Data 
18:369:30876:28:27:108:531:344:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:This section describes the variables we use to assess regime types, regime duration, and 
18:370:30965:27:28:72:543:317:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:property and contract rights.    Since both the regime type and regime duration variables have been 
18:371:31065:28:27:72:543:289:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:newly constructed for this paper and should ultimately also prove useful to other investigators, we 
18:372:31165:27:28:72:517:262:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:must describe them fully.    But the rest of the paper should be comprehensible even to those 
18:373:31259:28:28:72:259:234:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:readers who have skipped this section. 
18:374:31297:28:27:72:215:206:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:3.1. Defining Regime Types 
18:375:31323:27:28:108:516:179:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:Most recent empirical studies of democracy and economic performance make use of 
18:376:31403:28:28:72:527:151:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:Gastil's (1989) measures of political rights and/or civil liberties.    The Gastil measures include 
18:377:31502:28:0:72:520:123:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:some rights that are more nearly outcomes of political and economic processes than defining 
19:378:31596:0:27:72:543:675:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:features or requisites of a democratic political system.4  Given that our interest is in assessing the 
19:379:31699:27:28:72:539:648:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:impact of regime type on property rights, the outcomes-based nature of the Gastil indexes makes 
19:380:31795:28:27:72:530:620:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:them inappropriate indicators of democracy.    In addition, they do not cover part of our sample 
19:381:31892:27:446:72:108:593:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:period. 
19:382:31899:446:11:72:221:147:12:g_d0_f8:12:g_d0_f8:                               
19:383:31929:11:16:108:523:136:6:Times New Roman:10:Times New Roman:4  The civil liberties checklist includes "personal social rights, including those to property, internal and 
19:384:32037:16:11:72:531:120:10:Times New Roman:10:Times New Roman:external travel, choice of residence, marriage, and family," "freedom from gross social inequality," "freedom from 
19:385:32152:11:12:72:533:109:10:Times New Roman:10:Times New Roman:gross government indifference or corruption," and "socio-economic rights: including freedom from dependency on 
19:386:32263:12:11:72:520:97:10:Times New Roman:10:Times New Roman:landlords, bosses, union leaders, or bureaucrats."    The political rights checklist includes "recent shifts in power 
19:387:32381:11:0:72:486:86:10:Times New Roman:10:Times New Roman:through elections," "significant opposition vote," and "informal consensus: de facto opposition power." 
20:388:32486:0:27:108:530:675:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:Our definition of democracy is procedural.    In a democratic regime the chief executive 
20:389:32575:27:28:72:539:648:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:and the legislature are both elected in competitive elections and the legislature is effective, in the 
20:390:32678:28:27:72:531:620:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:sense that it has considerable autonomy.    In this definition both presidential and parliamentary 
20:391:32777:27:28:72:534:593:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:systems can be fully democratic.    A regime falls short of full democracy if the elections are not 
20:392:32877:28:27:72:543:565:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:fully competitive or if the executive's power is so predominant that the legislature does not provide 
20:393:32979:27:28:72:234:538:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:an effective check on that power. 
20:394:33012:28:28:108:528:510:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:Our definition of democracy is procedural, but the existence of competitive democratic 
20:395:33098:28:27:72:543:482:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:procedures implies the existence of certain rights.    It is obviously impossible for a society to have 
20:396:33202:27:28:72:504:455:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:continuing and truly competitive elections unless certain freedoms are maintained.    Thus 
20:397:33293:28:27:72:543:427:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:continuing representative government implies free speech, the right to campaign freely, the right to 
20:398:33394:27:28:72:536:400:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:form political parties, the right of peaceful demonstration, and freedom from arbitrary arrest.    It 
20:399:33496:28:28:72:488:372:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:also implies that at least some opponents of the party in power must be able to survive 
20:400:33584:28:27:72:535:344:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:economically, and thus have at least enough property and contract rights to remain viable.    The 
20:401:33682:27:28:72:543:317:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:only fully competitive elections are those in which even the opponents of the party in power have 
20:402:33780:28:27:72:299:289:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:the rights they need to compete and to survive. 
20:403:33827:27:28:108:512:262:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:A full-fledged dictatorship, on the other hand, is a regime in which neither the chief 
20:404:33914:28:28:72:537:234:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:executive nor the legislature (if one exists) is chosen in a competitive election, or one in which a 
20:405:34015:28:27:72:528:206:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:competitively-elected legislature is rendered ineffective by a non-elected (or not competitively 
20:406:34112:27:67:72:168:179:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:elected) executive.5 
20:407:34132:67:10:72:221:112:12:g_d0_f8:12:g_d0_f8:                               
20:408:34162:10:16:108:520:102:6:Times New Roman:10:Times New Roman:5  The definitions of democracy and dictatorship refer exclusively to the characteristics of the national 
20:409:34268:16:0:72:471:86:10:Times New Roman:10:Times New Roman:government.    We do not attempt to characterize the selection of officials at the sub-national levels. 
21:410:34373:0:27:108:515:675:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:We classify regimes by relying as much as possible on the judgments made by other 
21:411:34455:27:28:72:525:648:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:observers, although in a few situations we draw our own inferences in resolving ambiguities.   
21:412:34550:28:27:72:505:620:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:These instances are explained below.    Our basic sources for data on selection of the chief 
21:413:34643:27:28:72:538:593:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:executive and effectiveness of the legislature are Gurr's Polity II (1990) and Banks (1979).    Our 
21:414:34742:28:27:72:543:565:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:classification assigns a number from I to V to each country in each year, where these numbers have 
21:415:34841:27:28:72:191:538:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:the following meanings: 
21:416:34864:28:14:72:206:510:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman: I. Dictatorship 
21:417:34878:14:14:72:244:496:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman: II. Almost Dictatorship 
21:418:34900:14:13:72:254:482:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman: III. Intermediate Category 
21:419:34925:13:14:72:240:469:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman: IV. Almost Democracy 
21:420:34944:14:14:72:202:455:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman: V. Democracy 
21:421:34955:14:14:72:75:441:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman: 
21:422:34955:14:27:108:528:427:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:These classifications are based on the variables executive competitiveness (XRCOMP) 
21:423:35039:27:28:72:542:400:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:from Gurr and executive selection (EXSELEC) and legislative effectiveness (LEGEF) in Banks.   
21:424:35133:28:28:72:525:372:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:Gurr and Banks provide two alternative judgments about the selection of the chief executive.   
21:425:35228:28:27:72:528:344:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:Gurr's XRCOMP classifies countries into one of three categories with respect to how the chief 
21:426:35322:27:28:72:543:317:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:executive is selected.    These may be loosely described as (1) no elections or rigged elections; (2) 
21:427:35424:28:27:72:523:289:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:dual/transitional, where there are two executives or there is a transition between selection and 
21:428:35521:27:28:72:506:262:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:election; and (3) competitive election.    Banks' EXSELEC provides essentially a two-way 
21:429:35610:28:28:72:543:234:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:classification: the chief executive is either elected or not.    Banks' LEGEF classifies countries into 
21:430:35714:28:27:72:526:206:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:one of three categories with respect to the legislature: (1) no legislature or one that is rendered 
21:431:35814:27:28:72:543:179:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:completely ineffective by domestic turmoil or by the actions of the chief executive; (2) a partially 
21:432:35915:28:28:72:488:151:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:effective legislature; (3) an effective legislature, elected under competitive conditions. 
21:433:36005:28:27:108:492:123:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:Five categories (I-V) are derived from these variables in the following way.    A 
21:434:36087:27:0:72:517:96:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:full-fledged Democracy (V) is in the top category on all three variables, while a full-fledged 
22:435:36184:0:27:72:542:675:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:Dictatorship (I) is in the bottom category on XRCOMP and LEGEF.    An Almost Democracy (IV) 
22:436:36276:27:28:72:543:648:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:falls short of the top rating on either XRCOMP or LEGEF, while an Almost Dictatorship (II) is in 
22:437:36373:28:27:72:543:620:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:the intermediate category on LEGEF.    The other cases are classified in the Intermediate Category 
22:438:36472:27:28:72:542:593:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:(III), or are inconsistent (for example, because Gurr and Banks rate the chief executive differently, 
22:439:36574:28:27:72:543:565:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:or because the legislature is rated as fully effective yet the chief executive was selected rather than 
22:440:36678:27:28:72:537:538:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:elected).6  In our empirical tests below, we treat countries in categories IV or V as democracies, 
22:441:36777:28:28:72:488:510:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:and countries in categories I and II as autocracies.    The small number of country-year 
22:442:36866:28:27:72:267:482:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:observations in category III are omitted. 
22:443:36907:27:28:108:543:455:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:The Gurr and Banks data are available only through 1986.    Our research assistant Suzanne 
22:444:36998:28:27:72:543:427:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:Gleason updated regimes codings through 1990, relying primarily on the Europa Yearbook.    Only 
22:445:37094:27:28:72:478:400:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:seven countries were judged to have changed classification between 1986 and 1990. 
22:446:37175:28:28:108:480:372:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:Empirically, the differences between our procedural definition and the Gastil 
22:447:37253:28:27:72:535:344:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:outcomes-based measures turn out to be relatively minor.7  A crucial advantage of our measure 
22:448:37347:27:28:72:543:317:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:for present purposes is that the data it is based on are available well before the 1973 beginning date 
22:449:37450:28:32:72:170:289:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:for Gastil's indexes. 
22:450:37471:32:10:72:221:257:12:g_d0_f8:12:g_d0_f8:                               
22:451:37501:10:16:108:542:247:6:Times New Roman:10:Times New Roman:6  Our conception of democracy is fundamentally consistent with the conceptions of Bollen (1990) and other 
22:452:37608:16:12:72:542:231:10:Times New Roman:10:Times New Roman:political scientists who have adopted a procedural definition of democracy.    There is a conceptual difference, though, 
22:453:37729:12:11:72:537:219:10:Times New Roman:10:Times New Roman:between our scheme and those that add up the scores on different indicators.    Such a methodology assumes that the 
22:454:37845:11:12:72:546:208:10:Times New Roman:10:Times New Roman:contribution of a characteristic to the democratic nature of a regime is independent of the level of other characteristics.   
22:455:37971:12:11:72:542:196:10:Times New Roman:10:Times New Roman:However, the marginal productivity of an input (in this case, in producing democracy) usually depends on the level of 
22:456:38089:11:12:72:531:185:10:Times New Roman:10:Times New Roman:other inputs.    A dictator who tolerates freedom of the press during periods in which he feels secure in his position 
22:457:38208:12:11:72:532:173:10:Times New Roman:10:Times New Roman:does not on that account become a more democratic ruler.    Similarly, the fact that the ballots are counted honestly 
22:458:38326:11:12:72:529:162:10:Times New Roman:10:Times New Roman:does not make a regime more democratic if important political alternatives are prevented from participating in the 
22:459:38441:12:11:72:535:150:10:Times New Roman:10:Times New Roman:elections.    Our classification does not yield a ranking identical to one obtained from a mechanical adding up of the 
22:460:38560:11:19:72:506:139:10:Times New Roman:10:Times New Roman:scores on each of the component indicators.    See the Appendix for a summary of our classification scheme. 
22:461:38667:19:16:108:535:120:6:Times New Roman:10:Times New Roman:7  The simple Spearman rank-order correlations between our 5-category political regime indicator and the 
22:462:38772:16:12:72:541:104:10:Times New Roman:10:Times New Roman:7-point Gastil measures are quite high: 0.87 for political rights and 0.82 for civil liberties.    Changes in Gastil ratings 
22:463:38897:12:11:72:532:92:10:Times New Roman:10:Times New Roman:of countries over time are highly correlated with changes in our classification.    Correlations of each with property 
22:464:39016:11:0:72:206:81:10:Times New Roman:10:Times New Roman:rights indicators differ very little. 
23:465:39055:0:27:72:271:675:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:3.2. Measurement of Regime Duration 
23:466:39090:27:28:108:532:648:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:For democracies, we create two duration measures:    DEMDUR refers to the number of 
23:467:39174:28:27:72:502:620:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:consecutive years that a country has been a democracy8 (i.e., regime type IV or V), while 
23:468:39263:27:28:72:520:593:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:DEXDUR is the number of years that the chief executive has been in office in a democracy.   
23:469:39354:28:27:72:530:565:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:Thus, DEMDUR is reset to one in any year in which the country lapses from democratic status 
23:470:39446:27:28:72:542:538:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:(i.e., drops to category III or below), while DEXDUR is reset to one in any year in which the chief 
23:471:39546:28:28:72:165:510:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:executive changes. 
23:472:39564:28:27:108:542:482:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:For autocracies, the variable AUTDUR is defined as the number of consecutive years that 
23:473:39652:27:28:72:515:455:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:the chief executive in an autocratic nation has been in power.    The value of AUTDUR thus 
23:474:39743:28:27:72:542:427:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:increases by one for each year that the autocrat remains in power and the regime remains in either 
23:475:39841:27:28:72:529:400:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:of the categories I and II.    The variable is reset to one in any year in which the chief executive 
23:476:39942:28:28:72:543:372:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:changes.    This proxy for the time horizons of decision makers in autocracies fits the simplest and 
23:477:40043:28:27:72:507:344:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:most common type of modern autocracy: one-man rule with no established procedures for 
23:478:40129:27:193:72:129:317:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:succession. 
23:479:40140:193:11:72:221:124:12:g_d0_f8:12:g_d0_f8:                               
23:480:40170:11:16:108:533:113:6:Times New Roman:10:Times New Roman:8  Our data on property rights go back no further than 1969.    In measuring duration of regimes, we begin 
23:481:40277:16:11:72:535:97:10:Times New Roman:10:Times New Roman:counting in 1930.    Since we use the log of duration in regressions, neglecting to identify an earlier starting date for 
23:482:40399:11:0:72:452:86:10:Times New Roman:10:Times New Roman:democracy in the U.S., Britain, etc. affects our estimates for DEMDUR's impact only trivially. 
24:483:40495:0:27:108:543:675:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:There are, however, some cases for which this proxy for autocratic time horizons does not 
24:484:40585:27:28:72:531:648:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:apply.    Though autocracies are much less likely to be institutionalized than democracies, some 
24:485:40682:28:27:72:467:620:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:relatively autocratic or at least non-democratic regimes have achieved a degree of 
24:486:40765:27:28:72:529:593:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:institutionalization.    For these regimes, the duration of the chief executive will be a somewhat 
24:487:40864:28:27:72:488:565:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:noisy measure.    In exceptional cases, such as Mexico in the heyday of the PRI, where 
24:488:40951:27:28:72:486:538:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:institutionalization reaches levels that are not normally found outside of the advanced 
24:489:41039:28:28:72:511:510:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:democracies, the expected remaining duration of the President's rule is never more than his 
24:490:41131:28:27:72:499:482:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:institutionally given single term of six years, but the time horizon of the PRI's oligarchic 
24:491:41224:27:28:72:522:455:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:establishment has been far longer.    In the more general case of undemocratic and entrenched 
24:492:41318:28:27:72:542:427:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:ruling parties,9 the chief executive may be removed by the party's ruling council or Politburo while 
24:493:41418:27:28:72:522:400:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:the dictatorial rule of the party continues.    As in Saudi Arabia, the monarch often attains and 
24:494:41516:28:28:72:506:372:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:maintains power only with the backing of other members of the royal family.    For a chief 
24:495:41607:28:27:72:543:344:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:executive who intends to have his son succeed him in power, the autocratic planning horizon is so 
24:496:41705:27:28:72:543:317:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:long that any confiscation that reduces investment and thus future income and tax collections will 
24:497:41804:28:27:72:542:289:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:not be advantageous.    What is common to all of these cases is the presence of a "ruling group," a 
24:498:41904:27:28:72:525:262:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:family or party with an indefinitely long life span and thus a longer-run interest in the nation's 
24:499:42003:28:28:72:542:234:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:long-term economic performance than an individualistic    autocrat would have.    Autocratic ruling 
24:500:42103:28:36:72:503:206:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:groups usually also impose some constraints on the unilateral decisions of their leaders.10 
24:501:42194:36:10:72:221:170:12:g_d0_f8:12:g_d0_f8:                               
24:502:42224:10:16:108:542:160:6:Times New Roman:10:Times New Roman:9  In addition to Mexico, prominent examples include Taiwan and most communist countries (which are not 
24:503:42328:16:19:72:134:144:10:Times New Roman:10:Times New Roman:in our sample). 
24:504:42343:19:16:108:528:125:6:Times New Roman:10:Times New Roman:10  The chief of such a dictatorial party usually has little chance of success if he attempts to use society's 
24:505:42454:16:12:72:542:109:10:Times New Roman:10:Times New Roman:resources to maintain power in the face of widespread opposition within his party.    The costs of losing power are also 
24:506:42574:12:11:72:542:97:10:Times New Roman:10:Times New Roman:usually lower where autocracy is institutionalized, as the party can offer a deposed leader credible guarantees of a safe, 
24:507:42697:11:0:72:168:86:10:Times New Roman:10:Times New Roman:comfortable retirement. 
25:508:42722:0:27:108:519:675:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:These considerations lead us to adopt a second measure of tenure for autocracies, the 
25:509:42808:27:28:72:526:648:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:duration of the ruling group (AUTGROUP).    Whenever one autocrat is succeeded by another 
25:510:42898:28:27:72:538:620:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:autocrat belonging to the same "group," the counter variable AUTGROUP continues, rather than 
25:511:42991:27:28:72:530:593:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:re-starting at one, as AUTDUR does.    As with AUTDUR and DEMDUR, we hypothesize that 
25:512:43077:28:27:72:483:565:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:far-sighted policies regarding property rights will be associated with higher values of 
25:513:43165:27:28:72:517:538:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:AUTGROUP, our measure of stability of the ruling group.    In defining groups, our primary 
25:514:43255:28:28:72:533:510:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:criterion is the peaceful transfer of power.    Except in rare circumstances (such as an overthrow 
25:515:43354:28:27:72:525:482:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:within a ruling family, as in Oman in 1970), exit via a coup is regarded as a change in group.   
25:516:43451:27:28:72:534:455:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:Information from Europa Yearbook and other sources was used in judging the extent to which a 
25:517:43543:28:27:72:543:427:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:new leader represented a sharp break with his predecessor.    Monarchical succession, and transfers 
25:518:43643:27:28:72:543:400:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:of power within strong ruling parties (or revolutionary councils) were coded as occurring within a 
25:519:43741:28:28:72:462:372:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:given group.    In all, about 30 percent of transfers were judged to be intra-group. 
25:520:43825:28:28:72:75:344:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman: 
25:521:43825:28:27:72:230:316:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:3.3. Property Rights Measures 
25:522:43854:27:27:108:543:289:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:There are many ways in which governments can violate -- or fail to protect against private 
25:523:43944:27:28:72:497:262:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:theft and usurpation -- the property and contract rights of its citizens and subjects: direct 
25:524:44037:28:28:72:500:234:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:expropriation of assets, defaulting on public debt, debasing the currency, prohibiting any 
25:525:44128:28:27:72:503:206:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:transactions other than those at officially established prices, and failing to provide a legal 
25:526:44223:27:28:72:537:179:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:infrastructure that impartially enforces contracts and adjudicates disputes about property rights.   
25:527:44324:28:28:72:522:151:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:No one measure can capture all of these aspects of property and contract rights, so we use six 
25:528:44419:28:27:72:537:123:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:separate variables: the amount of "contract-intensive money" (defined below), indexes from two 
25:529:44514:27:0:72:499:96:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:firms evaluating risks to foreign investors, a subjective measure of default risk, currency 
26:530:44608:0:27:72:338:675:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:depreciation, and the black market exchange premium. 
26:531:44660:27:28:108:543:648:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:"Contract-intensive money" (CIM) is defined as (M2-C)/M2, where M2 is a broad definition 
26:532:44748:28:27:72:542:620:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:of money and C is currency outside banks.    In environments in which third-party enforcement of 
26:533:44845:27:28:72:531:593:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:contracts is reliable and where property rights facilitate pledging of assets as security for loans, 
26:534:44946:28:27:72:538:565:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:banks and other financial intermediaries will profit from providing retail banking services at low 
26:535:45045:27:28:72:542:538:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:cost, and sometimes even from paying interest on bank deposits, in order to obtain money that they 
26:536:45143:28:28:72:490:510:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:can lend at higher rates.    If the public can rely on institutional stability and third-party 
26:537:45238:28:27:72:537:482:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:enforcement of contracts, they can be confident that the banks or government will not confiscate 
26:538:45335:27:28:72:543:455:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:their deposits.    Thus the rationale for this measure is that those forms of money, such as currency, 
26:539:45438:28:27:72:511:427:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:that rely least on the fulfillment of contractual obligations by others will be preferred when 
26:540:45533:27:28:72:542:400:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:property and contractual rights are insecure, whereas other forms of money are more advantageous 
26:541:45630:28:28:72:538:372:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:for most purposes in environments with secure contract-enforcement and property rights.    Since 
26:542:45727:28:27:72:542:344:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:the non-currency components of M2 are, by definition, held in banks or other financial institutions, 
26:543:45827:27:28:72:532:317:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:poor contract enforcement and property rights imply that any advantages of using money in the 
26:544:45921:28:27:72:543:289:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:form of deposits in financial institutions are small and that there is also the risk that sums deposited 
26:545:46026:27:28:72:535:262:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:will not be recovered.    Thus the poorer contract-enforcement and other institutions in a society, 
26:546:46126:28:28:72:542:234:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:the smaller the proportion of contract-intensive money individuals will hold.    We have found the 
26:547:46225:28:27:72:529:206:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:proportion of contract-intensive money to be a useful and reliable measure in other contexts as 
26:548:46321:27:28:72:106:179:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:well.11
