26:549:46328:28:39:108:525:151:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:For two other measures of property rights, we employ ratings compiled by two private 
26:550:46413:39:10:72:221:112:12:g_d0_f8:12:g_d0_f8:                               
26:551:46443:10:16:108:510:102:6:Times New Roman:10:Times New Roman:11  For a more extensive description of and justification for CIM, and evidence on its relationship to 
26:552:46546:16:0:72:352:86:10:Times New Roman:10:Times New Roman:economic performance, see Clague, Keefer, Knack and Olson (1995). 
27:553:46613:0:27:72:542:675:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:firms for potential foreign investors.    Though these ratings are subjective, the firms that produced 
27:554:46716:27:28:72:532:648:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:them for sale had an incentive to make them as accurate as possible, and the fact that they were 
27:555:46813:28:27:72:521:620:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:purchased by investors who would lose from wrong information also adds something to their 
27:556:46903:27:28:72:531:593:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:credibility.    The International Country Risk Guide (ICRG), published since 1982, covers more 
27:557:46998:28:27:72:533:565:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:than 100 countries.    Business Environmental Risk Intelligence (BERI) has provided ratings for 
27:558:47094:27:28:72:257:538:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:about 50 countries beginning in 1972. 
27:559:47131:28:28:108:525:510:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:From five variables contained in one of these sources and four scored by the other, we 
27:560:47218:28:27:72:542:482:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:create the two simple additive indices, "ICRG" and "BERI."12  The five variables comprising the 
27:561:47314:27:28:72:511:455:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:ICRG index are "Expropriation Risk," "Risk of Contract Repudiation by the Government," 
27:562:47401:28:27:72:521:427:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:"Quality of the Bureaucracy," "Corruption in Government," and "Rule of Law."13  Variables 
27:563:47491:27:28:72:543:400:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:entering the BERI index include "Contract Enforceability," "Nationalization Risk," "Bureaucratic 
27:564:47588:28:28:72:264:372:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:Delays," and "Infrastructure Quality."14 
27:565:47628:28:27:108:543:344:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:"Contract Enforceability" by BERI and "Risk of Repudiation of Contracts by Government" 
27:566:47715:27:28:72:519:317:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:by ICRG are measures of how well contracts are enforced.    "Rule of Law" scores reflect the 
27:567:47808:28:27:72:530:289:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:strength of the court system and the degree to which citizens accept the lawmaking powers and 
27:568:47902:27:28:72:543:262:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:dispute resolution mechanisms of legal institutions, rather than depending on force or other illegal 
27:569:48003:28:40:72:486:234:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:means to settle claims.15  Definitions of "Corruption in Government," "Quality of the 
27:570:48089:40:11:72:221:194:12:g_d0_f8:12:g_d0_f8:                               
27:571:48119:11:16:108:542:183:6:Times New Roman:10:Times New Roman:12  These simple additive scales were found to be highly correlated (r > .99) with alternative scales weighted 
27:572:48230:16:19:72:265:167:10:Times New Roman:10:Times New Roman:by factor scores generated from factor analyses. 
27:573:48278:19:16:108:543:148:6:Times New Roman:10:Times New Roman:13  The latter 3 measures are scored on a 0-6 scale.    We multiply them by 10/6 to put them on the same 0-10 
27:574:48388:16:19:72:437:132:10:Times New Roman:10:Times New Roman:scale as the former 2 variables.    The resulting additive index has a potential range of 0-50. 
27:575:48483:19:16:108:542:113:6:Times New Roman:10:Times New Roman:14  Each variable is scored 0-4, with fractional values possible.    BERI scores are averages from a permanent 
27:576:48594:16:19:72:430:97:10:Times New Roman:10:Times New Roman:panel of experts, while ICRG ratings are evaluated by the staff of Political Risk Services. 
27:577:48685:19:0:108:539:78:6:Times New Roman:10:Times New Roman:15  High scores for "Rule of Law" also indicate "provisions for an orderly succession of power," raising the 
28:578:48795:0:27:72:534:675:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:Bureaucracy," "Bureaucratic Delays," and "Transportation and Communication Quality" justify 
28:579:48887:27:28:72:540:648:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:their use as measures of the general efficiency of provision of government services as well as the 
28:580:48986:28:461:72:351:620:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:extent of rent-seeking behavior of government officials.16 
28:581:49044:461:15:72:545:159:12:g_d0_f8:12:g_d0_f8:                                                                                                   
28:582:49142:15:12:72:535:144:10:Times New Roman:10:Times New Roman:possibility that correlations with regime type might be tautological.    Deleting "Rule of Law" from our ICRG index 
28:583:49258:12:19:72:488:132:10:Times New Roman:10:Times New Roman:does not change any results, however, as this alternative index is correlated with the one we use at .998. 
28:584:49364:19:16:108:515:113:6:Times New Roman:10:Times New Roman:16  See Knack and Keefer (1995) for more detailed definitions and discussion of the ICRG and BERI 
28:585:49462:16:11:72:519:97:10:Times New Roman:10:Times New Roman:variables.    Some of these variables may be taken as empirical proxies for Clague's concept of "rule obedience" 
28:586:49574:11:0:72:136:86:10:Times New Roman:10:Times New Roman:(Clague, 1993). 
29:587:49591:0:27:108:520:675:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:Our fourth measure of property and contract rights is a subjective rating of the risk of 
29:588:49680:27:28:72:515:648:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:default on sovereign debt.    This "credit rating" variable (CREDIT) can range from 0 to 100 
29:589:49773:28:27:72:534:620:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:(higher values indicate a lower risk of default, but values are not interpretable as probabilities).   
29:590:49876:27:28:72:494:593:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:This measure is an average of evaluations by a panel of international bankers published 
29:591:49964:28:27:72:273:565:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:semi-annually by Institutional Investor.17 
29:592:50006:27:28:108:534:538:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:Our fifth measure is the debasement of the currency as measured by the rate of currency 
29:593:50094:28:28:72:543:510:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:depreciation (DEPREC), which is equal to (100 + inflation rate)/100.    Inflation (as well as default 
29:594:50196:28:27:72:523:482:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:on the sovereign debt) can be viewed as an indirect method of expropriation, an alternative to 
29:595:50291:27:28:72:213:455:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:directly expropriating assets. 
29:596:50321:28:27:108:503:427:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:Our final measure is the (log of the) black market premium on currency exchange 
29:597:50401:27:28:72:542:400:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:(PREMIUM).    A high black market premium suggests that there are exchange controls and severe 
29:598:50496:28:28:72:534:372:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:import restrictions.    These controls and restrictions not only limit the types of contracts and the 
29:599:50598:28:27:72:542:344:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:uses of property that are permissible in a country, but also give government officials a wide range 
29:600:50698:27:28:72:524:317:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:of discretionary power through the granting or withholding of licenses and other permissions. 
29:601:50791:28:27:108:516:289:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:Each of the foregoing measures has its own idiosyncrasies, but to the extent they are 
29:602:50877:27:28:72:543:262:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:uncorrelated, they can be viewed as complementary.    Our empirical findings are not dependent on 
29:603:50974:28:28:72:253:234:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:the use of any one of these measures. 
29:604:51011:28:27:72:193:206:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:3.4. Control Variables  
29:605:51033:27:28:108:543:179:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:Given the dearth of empirical literature on the determinants of property rights, there are no 
29:606:51127:28:39:72:518:151:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:well-established precedents on model specification.    We include only (the log of) per capita 
29:607:51222:39:10:72:221:112:12:g_d0_f8:12:g_d0_f8:                               
29:608:51252:10:16:108:525:102:6:Times New Roman:10:Times New Roman:17  We use the mean of the two scores assigned each year (in March and September) to a country as the 
29:609:51353:16:0:72:188:86:10:Times New Roman:10:Times New Roman:country's value for that year. 
30:610:51385:0:27:72:542:675:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:income and time variables as regressors accompanying regime type and duration indicators in the 
30:611:51481:27:28:72:236:648:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:regressions reported in the tables. 
30:612:51516:28:27:108:517:620:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:Theoretical accounts of property rights claim that more is spent to define and protect 
30:613:51603:27:28:72:525:593:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:property rights when the rights themselves become more valuable.    Growth could make them 
30:614:51693:28:27:72:538:565:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:more valuable (Eggertsson, 1990).    Rosenberg and Birdzell (1986, pp. 115-117) have noted that 
30:615:51789:27:28:72:536:538:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:formal arrangements for protecting property rights, such as judicial systems based on precedent, 
30:616:51886:28:28:72:541:510:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:are not instituted until there is a sufficient volume of transactions to make them practicable.    We 
30:617:51988:28:27:72:528:482:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:can imperfectly control for these effects by including per capita income and aggregate GDP as 
30:618:52082:27:28:72:519:455:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:proxies for the value of assets and volume of transactions.18  One might alternatively posit a 
30:619:52177:28:27:72:527:427:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:threshold effect, whereby for example a legal system is instituted when the value of assets and 
30:620:52273:27:28:72:541:400:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:volume of transactions imply that the social benefits of setting up courts exceed the social costs.   
30:621:52375:28:28:72:516:372:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:Casual observation does not support such a view -- even in very small developing countries, 
30:622:52466:28:27:72:536:344:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:increased expenditures on courts would surely pass such a cost-benefit test19  --  and we do not 
30:623:52563:27:158:72:194:317:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:test for threshold effects. 
30:624:52590:158:11:72:221:159:12:g_d0_f8:12:g_d0_f8:                               
30:625:52620:11:16:108:517:148:6:Times New Roman:10:Times New Roman:18  Aggregate GDP is generally not a significant determinant of our property rights measures, and has 
30:626:52722:16:11:72:542:132:10:Times New Roman:10:Times New Roman:virtually no impact on coefficients for regime type and duration variables.    Thus, regressions reported in tables below 
30:627:52844:11:19:72:185:121:10:Times New Roman:10:Times New Roman:do not include this variable. 
30:628:52872:19:16:108:514:102:6:Times New Roman:10:Times New Roman:19  In Egypt, many courts do not operate much during the summer months due to a simple lack of air 
30:629:52971:16:0:72:272:86:10:Times New Roman:10:Times New Roman:conditioning (Washington Post, March 13, 1995). 
31:630:53020:0:27:108:543:675:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:The close historical connection between the emergence of democratic political institutions 
31:631:53111:27:28:72:543:648:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:and the development of property and contract rights poses problems for testing the causal effects of 
31:632:53212:28:27:72:539:620:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:one upon the other.    A consensus is forming on the view that secure property and contract rights 
31:633:53311:27:28:72:527:593:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:are important facilitators of economic growth.    Thus a high level of income in a society today 
31:634:53408:28:27:72:543:565:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:suggests that there were good property and contract rights in the past.    Given the persistence of the 
31:635:53512:27:28:72:518:538:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:institutions that sustain property and contract rights, income is also a good predictor of these 
31:636:53609:28:28:72:529:510:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:institutions.    Moreover, there are many aspects of a political regime that influence growth and 
31:637:53707:28:27:72:500:482:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:hence, over time, the level of income.    These include bureaucratic competence, political 
31:638:53798:27:28:72:521:455:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:legitimacy, and rule obedience, on the one hand, and susceptibilities to political violence and 
31:639:53894:28:27:72:543:427:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:extreme inequalities, on the other.    These characteristics also tend to persist.    Thus a high level of 
31:640:54001:27:28:72:538:400:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:income in a society today usually means that there was a well-functioning political regime in the 
31:641:54099:28:28:72:537:372:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:past, and, because of persistence of these characteristics, it also increases the probability that the 
31:642:54202:28:27:72:307:344:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:current political regime also has these attributes. 
31:643:54253:27:28:108:542:317:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:What makes our empirical analysis of the effects of political regimes possible is that there 
31:644:54346:28:27:72:543:289:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:are some independent forces producing changes in political regime.    In particular there have been 
31:645:54446:27:28:72:548:262:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:wars won by democracies, after which democracies were set up in countries that had lacked them.   
31:646:54544:28:28:72:543:234:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:More importantly for our sample, massive decolonization has occurred, as well as other historical 
31:647:54642:28:27:72:370:206:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:factors that have altered many countries' political institutions. 
31:648:54707:27:28:108:543:179:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:But it remains true that current period income contains much information about the current 
31:649:54798:28:28:72:537:151:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:state of property rights and political regime.    Since our analysis controls for current income and 
31:650:54899:28:27:72:527:123:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:necessarily employs relatively crude measures of political regimes to investigate the impact of 
31:651:54995:27:0:72:406:96:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:political conditions on property rights, our tests are quite demanding. 
32:652:55068:0:27:108:534:675:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:There are some secular and exogenous developments that may also affect the security of 
32:653:55155:27:28:72:543:648:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:property and contract rights.    The proportion of contract-intensive money (CIM) may be sensitive 
32:654:55254:28:27:72:504:620:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:to advances in banking technology that lower the costs of intermediation.    For subjective 
32:655:55346:27:28:72:530:593:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:measures that have ceilings on the maximum possible scores, each country might be rated with 
32:656:55439:28:27:72:541:565:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:reference to other countries at a given point in time: mean scores for the world could then remain 
32:657:55538:27:28:72:543:538:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:constant even with a general improvement over time in the security of property and contract rights 
32:658:55636:28:28:72:528:510:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:around the world.    To avoid spuriously associating such changes, or nonchanges, with regime 
32:659:55730:28:27:72:515:482:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:type and duration, time (equal to the current year minus 1969) is included as an explanatory 
32:660:55823:27:28:72:124:455:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:variable.20 
32:661:55834:28:27:108:505:427:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:The proportion of contract-intensive money (CIM) might seem likely to be greatly 
32:662:55915:27:28:72:522:400:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:influenced by inflation and interest rates (Clague et al., 1995).    In fact, the inclusion of these 
32:663:56016:28:28:72:511:372:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:variables has only a minute impact on the coefficients for regime type and duration in CIM 
32:664:56107:28:27:72:432:344:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:equations.    They are accordingly not included in the results reported here. 
32:665:56184:27:28:108:538:317:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:Inequalities in income and wealth and other social cleavages based on ethnicity, religion, 
32:666:56275:28:27:72:543:289:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:or region may generate social conflict endangering individual rights.    Similarly, culture, religion, 
32:667:56378:27:28:72:543:262:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:and colonial heritage may influence property and contractual rights.    We do not include measures 
32:668:56477:28:28:72:528:234:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:of these as regressors, however.    For our sample, the coverage of available data over time and 
32:669:56574:28:27:72:539:206:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:across countries on inequality and other social cleavages is inadequate.    Existing theories do not 
32:670:56675:27:28:72:543:179:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:account for the differences in the apparent effects of cultural variables across regions or over time: 
32:671:56778:28:26:72:539:151:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:why did British influences lead to strong property rights regimes only in some former colonies?   
32:672:56876:26:14:72:221:125:12:g_d0_f8:12:g_d0_f8:                               
32:673:56906:14:23:108:543:111:6:Times New Roman:10:g_d0_f8:20  Results using the log of time were very similar.    In fixed effects regressions, we use 
32:674:56998:23:0:72:228:88:10:g_d0_f8:10:Times New Roman:year dummies instead of time. 
33:675:57029:0:27:72:503:675:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:Why was "Confucianism" until relatively recently thought to be unfavorable to economic 
33:676:57116:27:28:72:533:648:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:development?    Also, since others have used cultural and heritage indicators to explain political 
33:677:57215:28:27:72:543:620:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:freedoms (Bhalla, 1994; Abrams and Lewis, 1993), inclusion of these variables as regressors along 
33:678:57313:27:28:72:543:593:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:with regime type would potentially confound tests of the latter's impact on property rights.    In any 
33:679:57416:28:27:72:532:565:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:event, to the extent that inequality, other social cleavages, culture, and colonial heritage remain 
33:680:57516:27:28:72:514:538:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:constant over time, their effects are captured by country intercepts in our fixed effects tests. 
33:681:57612:28:28:72:396:510:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:4. Property and Contract Rights in Different Types of Regimes 
33:682:57673:28:27:108:536:482:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:Some recent and sophisticated statistical studies on postwar data have supported Lipset's 
33:683:57763:27:28:72:542:455:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:(1959) thesis that high incomes are conducive to the emergence and survival of democracy (Barro, 
33:684:57860:28:27:72:540:427:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:1994; Burkhart and Lewis-Beck, 1994; Helliwell, 1994).    By contrast, there is no clear tendency 
33:685:57958:27:28:72:529:400:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:that has yet emerged from studies of the effects of democracy on economic performance.    The 
33:686:58052:28:28:72:543:372:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:three studies just cited conclude that democracy has either no influence or a negative influence on 
33:687:58152:28:27:72:543:344:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:subsequent growth.    A recent study by Bhalla (1994), on the other hand, finds a positive effect of 
33:688:58253:27:28:72:535:317:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:political rights on growth.21  Consistent with Bhalla's results is evidence from earlier periods of 
33:689:58353:28:27:72:506:289:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:history suggesting that representative or at least non-absolutist government is favorable to 
33:690:58446:27:28:72:353:262:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:economic performance (e.g., de Long and Shleifer, 1992). 
33:691:58502:28:28:108:492:234:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:We focus here on one of the proposed links between regime type and economic 
33:692:58578:28:27:72:509:206:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:performance: the hypothesis that more democratic regimes will better protect property and 
33:693:58668:27:32:72:529:179:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:contract rights.    We have elsewhere documented the impact of property and contract rights on 
33:694:58763:32:11:72:221:147:12:g_d0_f8:12:g_d0_f8:                               
33:695:58793:11:16:108:541:136:6:Times New Roman:10:Times New Roman:21  The difference in results between Bhalla and the other three studies appears to relate mainly to the choice 
33:696:58905:16:11:72:542:120:10:Times New Roman:10:Times New Roman:of other independent variables and instruments for democracy.    We focus on these four studies because they make use 
33:697:59023:11:12:72:542:109:10:Times New Roman:10:Times New Roman:of the most recent data on a large number of countries and because they pay careful attention to endogeneity problems, 
33:698:59142:12:11:72:534:97:10:Times New Roman:10:Times New Roman:mainly through the use of instrumental and lagged variables.    The earlier literature is also thoroughly inconclusive 
33:699:59261:11:0:72:508:86:10:Times New Roman:10:Times New Roman:regarding the effects of democracy on growth.    See, for examples, the review in Brunetti and Weder (1993). 
34:700:59371:0:27:72:438:675:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:investment and growth rates (Clague et al., 1995; Knack and Keefer, 1995). 
34:701:59445:27:28:108:512:648:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:The effects of regime type -- and of regime duration -- were first tested with pooled 
34:702:59529:28:27:72:542:620:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:time-series cross-sectional regressions, using country-years as units of analysis.    Results of these 
34:703:59631:27:28:72:525:593:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:tests were very supportive of the hypotheses.22  Errors from these regressions, however, were 
34:704:59725:28:27:72:543:565:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:highly autocorrelated, indicating that it is inappropriate to treat yearly observations of a country as 
34:705:59829:27:28:72:136:538:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:independent. 
34:706:59841:28:28:108:538:510:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:In a purely cross-sectional design, on the other hand, difficulties arise in assigning values 
34:707:59935:28:27:72:510:482:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:for regime type for countries moving across categories one or more times over the period.   
34:708:60027:27:28:72:524:455:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:Averaging the different regime types -- i.e., treating a country shifting from type II to type IV 
34:709:60124:28:27:72:527:427:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:halfway through the period identically to one remaining a category III over the entire period -- 
34:710:60220:27:28:72:526:400:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:would unjustifiably impose cardinality on our regime type index as well as fail to make use of 
34:711:60315:28:28:72:228:372:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:important variations in the data. 
34:712:60348:28:27:108:497:344:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:We adopted two alternative solutions.    First, we created an observation for each 
34:713:60431:27:28:72:532:317:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:country-regime, i.e. for each spell of democracy (for regressions with DEMDUR), and for each 
34:714:60524:28:27:72:535:289:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:period that a particular autocrat rules (for AUTDUR).23  With country-regime units of analysis, 
34:715:60620:27:28:72:533:262:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:we retained some over-time variation across regime types within countries, but suffered far less 
34:716:60717:28:28:72:510:234:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:serious autocorrelation problems (as confirmed by Durbin-Watson statistics).    Second, we 
34:717:60808:28:27:72:515:206:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:retained country-year units of analysis but incorporated fixed country and/or regime effects, 
34:718:60902:27:20:72:489:179:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:thereby arguably removing the most important sources of possible autocorrelation and 
34:719:60987:20:11:72:221:159:12:g_d0_f8:12:g_d0_f8:                               
34:720:61017:11:23:108:292:148:6:Times New Roman:10:Times New Roman:22  Results available on request from authors. 
34:721:61063:23:16:108:532:125:6:Times New Roman:10:Times New Roman:23  Thus, Egypt in 1954-1969, 1970-80, and 1981-1990 (1990 is the last year for our regimes and income 
34:722:61166:16:12:72:534:109:10:Times New Roman:10:Times New Roman:data) constitute three separate observations in Table 1 and in the AUTDUR panel of Table 3.    In the AUTGROUP 
34:723:61277:12:11:72:532:97:10:Times New Roman:10:Times New Roman:panel of Table 3, Egypt 1954-90 is one observation as Nasser, Sadat, and Mubarak are all judged to be of the same 
34:724:61391:11:0:72:107:86:10:Times New Roman:10:Times New Roman:"group." 
35:725:61401:0:27:72:164:675:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:heteroskedasticity. 
35:726:61420:27:28:108:513:648:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:Table 1 presents cross-sectional regressions, using country-regime units of analysis, 
35:727:61506:28:27:72:543:620:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:examining the effects of regime type on property rights (mean values over the period), controlling 
35:728:61605:27:28:72:530:593:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:for mean per capita income and mean time over the period the country-regime lasts.24  In each 
35:729:61699:28:27:72:529:565:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:case we find democracies outperforming autocracies, even controlling for the higher per capita 
35:730:61794:27:28:72:539:538:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:incomes prevailing in most democracies.    The Autocracy coefficient has the expected sign in all 
35:731:61892:28:28:72:495:510:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:six cases: negative for CIM, ICRG, BERI, and CREDIT, and positive for DEPREC and 
35:732:61973:28:27:72:543:482:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:PREMIUM.    These coefficients are highly significant for two of these property rights variables.   
35:733:62073:27:28:72:541:455:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:Higher incomes are associated with significantly better scores on each of the dependent variables 
35:734:62171:28:27:72:527:427:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:with the exception of DEPREC.    The latter, along with PREMIUM and CIM, all significantly 
35:735:62262:27:28:72:524:400:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:increase with time, controlling for income and regime type.    The time trend in CIM probably 
35:736:62356:28:28:72:543:372:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:reflects secular improvements in banking technology.    Negative coefficients for time on CREDIT 
35:737:62453:28:27:72:539:344:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:and (in some specifications) BERI suggest that scores for these variables reflect only the relative 
35:738:62553:27:170:72:297:317:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:positions of countries at a single point in time. 
35:739:62602:170:11:72:221:147:12:g_d0_f8:12:g_d0_f8:                               
35:740:62632:11:16:108:525:136:6:Times New Roman:10:Times New Roman:24  "Time" = year - 1969.    Where there is missing data on a dependent variable for some years within a 
35:741:62736:16:11:72:521:120:10:Times New Roman:10:Times New Roman:country-regime, we delete time and income data for the corresponding years.    Calculating mean time and mean 
35:742:62846:11:12:72:533:109:10:Times New Roman:10:Times New Roman:income for Franco's regime using all available data from the 1930s onward would yield means far below those that 
35:743:62959:12:11:72:531:97:10:Times New Roman:10:Times New Roman:actually apply to (for example) the 1972-90 period covered by BERI.    Then, income and time would underpredict 
35:744:63071:11:0:72:450:86:10:Times New Roman:10:Times New Roman:BERI, and positive BERI residuals would be spuriously associated with a high duration value. 
36:745:63165:0:27:108:542:675:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:The finding that democracies as a group outperform autocracies in protecting property and 
36:746:63254:27:28:72:535:648:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:contractual rights does not, if the arguments at the beginning of this article are right, necessarily 
36:747:63356:28:27:72:509:620:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:imply that the short- or medium-term effects of    shift from autocracy to democracy are an 
36:748:63447:27:28:72:542:593:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:improvement in performance.    To explore this issue, we shift to country-year units of analysis, to 
36:749:63547:28:27:72:532:565:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:exploit the time-series variation in the data, and control for fixed country-specific effects.    The 
36:750:63649:27:28:72:542:538:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:autocracy coefficient under this approach is influenced only by over-time variation in regime type 
36:751:63748:28:28:72:519:510:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:and property rights.    Given the length of our sample period (9 to 22 years, depending on the 
36:752:63843:28:27:72:528:482:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:dependent variable), this test is designed to reveal short- or medium-term effects of changes in 
36:753:63939:27:28:72:543:455:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:regime type on our property rights variables.    Estimates from country-regime regressions in Table 
36:754:64039:28:27:72:519:427:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:1 are heavily influenced by democracies of long standing, in Western Europe and among the 
36:755:64129:27:28:72:528:400:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:English-speaking nations.    No nation remaining a democracy (or an autocracy) over the entire 
36:756:64224:28:28:72:542:372:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:sample period influences the autocracy coefficients in Table 2; those estimates are based solely on 
36:757:64323:28:27:72:529:344:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:over-time variation within countries.    Results for the autocracy dummy in Table 2 are thus the 
36:758:64420:27:28:72:514:317:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:product of a relatively small number of countries with inter-regime shifts during the sample 
36:759:64513:28:27:72:116:289:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:period.25 
36:760:64522:27:28:108:526:262:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:The results summarized in Table 2 strongly indicate that new democracies tend to face 
36:761:64608:28:28:72:532:234:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:many of the difficulties, outlined earlier in the paper, that can render property rights less secure 
36:762:64709:28:27:72:529:206:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:than in a country ruled by a secure autocrat.    Autocracy is associated with significantly higher 
36:763:64808:27:28:72:539:179:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:CIM and BERI values, and significantly lower inflation (coefficients on the other three variables 
36:764:64906:28:39:72:532:151:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:are not significant).    Many of the benefits of democracy seem to accrue only over a substantial 
36:765:65004:39:10:72:221:112:12:g_d0_f8:12:g_d0_f8:                               
36:766:65034:10:16:108:536:102:6:Times New Roman:10:Times New Roman:25  During our sample period eight countries shifted from autocracy to democracy, two shifted in the other 
36:767:65141:16:0:72:341:86:10:Times New Roman:10:Times New Roman:direction, and eleven more experienced multiple shifts (e.g. Chile). 
37:768:65211:0:27:72:535:675:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:period of time, which may exceed the duration of most new democracies installed in our sample 
37:769:65305:27:28:72:543:648:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:period.    Most importantly, longstanding democracies, unlike all other regimes, have a predictable 
37:770:65405:28:27:72:532:620:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:succession of power.    They also tend to have more effective checks on executive power, in the 
37:771:65501:27:28:72:543:593:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:form of independent legislatures, central banks, and judiciaries, and this makes it more difficult for 
37:772:65604:28:27:72:513:565:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:any leader to abridge property or contract rights.26  In new democracies such as Argentina, 
37:773:65696:27:28:72:535:538:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:Nigeria (abortively), and Pakistan, by contrast, individuals cannot enter into long-term contracts 
37:774:65795:28:28:72:519:510:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:secure in the knowledge that successions will be orderly and legal, and that a chief executive 
37:775:65890:28:370:72:367:482:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:cannot preempt the powers of other branches of government. 
37:776:65948:370:10:72:221:112:12:g_d0_f8:12:g_d0_f8:                               
37:777:65978:10:16:108:542:102:6:Times New Roman:10:Times New Roman:26  In the U.S., the role of the Supreme Court as a check on unconstitutional actions of the Congress was not 
37:778:66088:16:0:72:449:86:10:Times New Roman:10:Times New Roman:established, nor recognized, until Marbury v. Madison, decided during Jefferson's presidency. 
38:779:66183:0:27:108:537:675:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:In addition to the uncertainty and instability pervading new democracies generally, other 
38:780:66273:27:28:72:508:648:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:factors potentially contribute to the positive Autocracy coefficients in Table 2.    First, new 
38:781:66369:28:27:72:532:620:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:democracies in recent years are hardly a random sample of all democracies.    These "marginal" 
38:782:66464:27:28:72:528:593:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:democracies exhibit a substantially worse income distribution, more ethnic tensions, and more 
38:783:66558:28:27:72:531:565:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:political violence than exhibited by countries remaining democracies throughout the 1970s and 
38:784:66652:27:28:72:537:538:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:80s.    Prevailing social conditions often subject these new democracies to extraordinary populist 
38:785:66751:28:28:72:516:510:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:pressures, which autocrats in these same countries were (sometimes) better able to resist.27  
38:786:66845:28:27:72:543:482:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:Second, democracies are more likely to replace successful autocracies.    Autocracies almost never 
38:787:66944:27:28:72:543:455:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:replace democracies unless the latter are performing poorly -- when their legitimacy in the eyes of 
38:788:67043:28:27:72:542:427:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:the public is especially low.    Conversely, with the exception of Argentina, autocrats giving way to 
38:789:67145:27:28:72:537:400:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:new democratic regimes during our sample period apparently chose to do so when the economic 
38:790:67237:28:28:72:539:372:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:climate was favorable for a smooth transition to democracy (as in Chile, Uruguay, and Turkey).   
38:791:67334:28:27:72:523:344:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:Given these selection processes, the autocracy coefficient in fixed-effects tests is conceivably 
38:792:67430:27:28:72:494:317:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:capturing a regression-to-the-mean effect: autocrats succeeding democracies have more 
38:793:67516:28:27:72:532:289:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:opportunity to improve the policy climate than do leaders of democracies succeeding autocrats. 
38:794:67610:27:28:72:75:262:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman: 
38:795:67610:28:87:72:283:234:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:5. Property Rights and Regime Duration 
38:796:67648:87:11:72:221:147:12:g_d0_f8:12:g_d0_f8:                               
38:797:67678:11:16:108:542:136:6:Times New Roman:10:Times New Roman:27  Keefer and Knack (1995) find that income distribution is a more important determinant of property rights 
38:798:67787:16:11:72:525:120:10:Times New Roman:10:Times New Roman:and risk of loan defaults in democracies than in autocracies.    Persson and Tabellini (1994) find that inequality is 
38:799:67905:11:12:72:534:109:10:Times New Roman:10:Times New Roman:harmful to growth, particularly in democracies.   One could alternatively interpret a significant interaction between 
38:800:68023:12:11:72:529:97:10:Times New Roman:10:Times New Roman:democracy and inequality in growth equations as implying that democracy is beneficial to growth where and only 
38:801:68134:11:0:72:325:86:10:Times New Roman:10:Times New Roman:where there exists a suitably egalitarian distribution of income. 
39:802:68201:0:27:108:543:675:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:For the reasons set out at the beginning of this paper, we hypothesize that the length of time 
39:803:68296:27:28:72:490:648:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:a democratic system has survived and the time horizons of each autocrat are important 
39:804:68382:28:27:72:520:620:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:determinants of the effects of regime type on property and contract rights.    If these temporal 
39:805:68479:27:28:72:492:593:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:considerations are as important as we expect them to be, any comparisons of economic 
39:806:68564:28:27:72:536:565:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:performance under autocracy and democracy that leave them out are likely to be mis-specified.   
39:807:68660:27:28:72:540:538:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:The same is true for the comparisons of property and contract rights under differing regime types 
39:808:68757:28:28:72:192:510:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:in the preceding section. 
39:809:68782:28:27:108:543:482:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:In this section, we test our hypotheses about how duration of regime affects the security of 
39:810:68875:27:28:72:542:455:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:property and contract rights in each type of regime.    That is, we test our hypothesis that autocrats 
39:811:68978:28:27:72:528:427:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:with longer duration will be associated with better property and contract rights than short-term 
39:812:69075:27:28:72:543:400:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:autocrats, and our hypothesis that the longer a democratic system has lasted the better these rights 
39:813:69176:28:28:72:111:372:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:will be. 
39:814:69184:28:27:108:547:344:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:Table 3 regressions test for the impact of regime duration on the security of property rights.   
39:815:69281:27:28:72:538:317:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:As with Table 1, cross-sectional regressions using country-regime units are reported in Table 3.   
39:816:69380:28:27:72:543:289:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:Control variables include mean income and time.    Autocracies and democracies are separated for 
39:817:69477:27:28:72:362:262:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:these tests, as duration is defined differently for each group. 
39:818:69540:28:28:108:543:234:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:The coefficient for duration of autocrats (AUTDUR) -- specifically, the log of duration the 
39:819:69631:28:27:72:503:206:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:year the regime ends -- has the expected sign in every case in Table 3, with three of these 
39:820:69722:27:28:72:541:179:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:statistically significant at .05 or better.    Results are similar for AUTGROUP, with better policies 
39:821:69824:28:28:72:534:151:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:associated with higher duration of the ruling group in every case, and significant associations in 
39:822:69923:28:27:72:130:123:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:three cases. 
39:823:69935:27:0:108:528:96:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:Coefficients for the duration of democratic regimes (DEMDUR) are all in the expected 
40:824:70022:0:27:72:541:675:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:direction, with three significant at the .05 level.    These generally favorable results on DEMDUR 
40:825:70121:27:28:72:535:648:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:are consistent with the view that new democracies cannot offer investors the same predictability 
40:826:70217:28:27:72:475:620:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:(of succession) and credibility (of policy) offered by the longstanding democracies. 
40:827:70301:27:28:108:539:593:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:This emphasis on the importance of the duration of democratic systems does not apply to 
40:828:70389:28:27:72:520:565:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:the tenure of particular leaders of democracies.    While policy making in democracies is not   
40:829:70484:27:28:72:542:538:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:immune to the short-term needs of chief executives with limited time horizons, there are far more 
40:830:70582:28:28:72:516:510:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:powerful checks on the ability of chief executives in democracies, compared to autocrats, to 
40:831:70675:28:27:72:354:482:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:expropriate assets, to renege on debts, and to print money. 
40:832:70734:27:28:108:542:455:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:The results in Table 3 support the view that the duration of democracy itself matters more 
40:833:70825:28:27:72:542:427:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:than the time in power of chief executives in democracies.    For these tests, we define democratic 
40:834:70925:27:28:72:526:400:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:leader regimes similarly to autocratic regimes: each unit of analysis corresponds to the time in 
40:835:71021:28:28:72:542:372:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:power of a chief executive.    For all six dependent variables, the effect of a one-year increase in the 
40:836:71126:28:27:72:543:344:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:duration of a democratic leader (DEXDUR) has a smaller impact (see fourth panel of Table 3) than 
40:837:71223:27:28:72:398:317:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:an identical increase in the duration of democracy (see third panel). 
40:838:71292:28:27:108:543:289:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:Our theory also suggests that the impact of DEXDUR should be weaker than the impact of 
40:839:71379:27:28:72:527:262:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:AUTDUR -- the duration of autocratic leaders.    The estimated impacts of leader duration are   
40:840:71474:28:28:72:524:234:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:similar, however, for autocrats and for democratic chief executives in the cross-sectional tests 
40:841:71571:28:27:72:543:206:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:reported in Table 3.    The results from fixed-effects models reported below, on the other hand, are 
40:842:71672:27:28:72:194:179:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:supportive of our theory. 
40:843:71697:28:28:108:543:151:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:Table 4 illustrates the economic significance of results in Table 3 by substituting values for 
40:844:71791:28:27:72:543:123:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:time, income and duration into the regressions to determine the predicted values of property rights 
40:845:71891:27:0:72:543:96:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:indicators.    The values in each cell correspond to predicted values of the property rights variables 
41:846:71996:0:27:72:541:675:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:with time = 11 (i.e., 1980) and per capita income of $2500.    Within each row, duration increases 
41:847:72095:27:28:72:543:648:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:from 2 to 10 to 25.    For each dependent variable, there are four rows, corresponding to autocratic 
41:848:72196:28:27:72:518:620:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:leaders, autocrat "groups," democratic leaders, and democratic regimes.    The most dramatic 
41:849:72289:27:28:72:538:593:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:improvements associated with increasing duration occur for the democratic regimes, particularly 
41:850:72385:28:27:72:520:565:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:for ICRG, DEPREC, and PREMIUM.    Focusing on the column for which duration = 2, new 
41:851:72470:27:28:72:519:538:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:autocrats have "better" values than new democracies on four of the six dependent variables.   
41:852:72564:28:28:72:543:510:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:However, democratic regimes lasting 25 years outscore autocrats of 25 years duration on four out 
41:853:72661:28:27:72:543:482:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:of six measures.    While many democracies surpass 25 years in duration, there is an upper limit to 
41:854:72761:27:28:72:508:455:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:how long an individual autocrat can last.    These results are consistent with the theory that 
41:855:72856:28:27:72:394:427:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:longstanding democracies provide the most secure property rights. 
41:856:72921:27:28:108:542:400:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:We further explore the effects of duration variables using fixed-effects regressions.    With 
41:857:73015:28:28:72:541:372:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:the cross-sectional design of Table 3 regressions, we cannot rule out unobserved country-specific 
41:858:73113:28:27:72:542:344:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:variables that may be responsible for both high rates of leadership turnover and insecure property 
41:859:73212:27:28:72:530:317:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:and contractual rights.    By including country dummies in regressions using the full time series 
41:860:73310:28:27:72:538:289:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:available, we can examine the influence of variations in the duration of leaders over time, within 
41:861:73409:27:28:72:286:262:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:countries, on the property rights variables.28 
41:862:73455:28:28:108:539:234:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:In five out of six cases (all except CREDIT), increases in autocratic duration (AUTDUR) 
41:863:73543:28:36:72:539:206:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:are associated with highly significant improvements in our property and contract rights measures 
41:864:73640:36:11:72:221:170:12:g_d0_f8:12:g_d0_f8:                               
41:865:73670:11:16:108:532:159:6:Times New Roman:10:Times New Roman:28  Results on the log of autocrat duration are generally weaker when regime dummies are substituted for 
41:866:73775:16:11:72:542:143:10:Times New Roman:10:Times New Roman:country dummies.    Regime effects are highly correlated within countries, and add very little explanatory power over 
41:867:73893:11:12:72:542:132:10:Times New Roman:10:Times New Roman:the country intercepts.    The major difference between the two models is that within a regime (as opposed to a country) 
41:868:74014:12:11:72:537:120:10:Times New Roman:10:Times New Roman:over time, duration always increases -- when a new autocrat comes into power, duration re-starts at 1.    As time and 
41:869:74131:11:12:72:515:109:10:Times New Roman:10:Times New Roman:(usually) income also increase each year, there are potentially serious multicollinearity problems using regime 
41:870:74243:12:11:72:521:97:10:Times New Roman:10:Times New Roman:dummies.    (Using time, as opposed to year dummies, and duration, as opposed to its log, would in fact result in 
41:871:74357:11:0:72:155:86:10:Times New Roman:10:Times New Roman:perfect collinearity.) 
42:872:74381:0:27:72:502:675:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:within countries (Table 5, first panel).    By contrast, increases in the duration of the chief 
42:873:74477:27:28:72:543:648:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:executive's leadership in democracies (DEXDUR) are associated with significant improvement in 
42:874:74571:28:27:72:542:620:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:only one of the six (CREDIT), with DEXDUR's coefficient taking on the wrong sign in four cases 
42:875:74666:27:28:72:533:593:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:(see third panel of Table 5).    Table 6 presents marginal effects for duration values as estimated 
42:876:74766:28:464:72:533:565:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:from Table 5 regressions, for changes in duration from 2 to 10 years, and from 10 to 25 years.29 
42:877:74862:464:11:72:221:101:12:g_d0_f8:12:g_d0_f8:                               
42:878:74892:11:0:108:446:90:6:Times New Roman:10:Times New Roman:29  We do not calculate predicted values because of the differing country intercepts. 
43:879:74979:0:27:108:527:675:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:By pooling the autocratic and democratic observations, and constructing an interaction 
43:880:75066:27:28:72:538:648:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:term equal to the autocracy dummy multiplied by the duration of the chief executive, we can test 
43:881:75162:28:27:72:522:620:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:whether differences between autocracies and democracies in the impact of leader duration on 
43:882:75254:27:28:72:534:593:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:property rights are statistically significant.    Coefficients on these interaction terms indicate that 
43:883:75358:28:27:72:543:565:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:more time in power for an autocrat improves property and contract rights more than does a longer 
43:884:75455:27:28:72:543:538:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:time in office for a democratic leader; the interactions are highly significant for CIM and the BERI 
43:885:75556:28:28:72:537:510:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:index, and significant at .05 or .06 levels for ICRG, DEPREC, and PREMIUM.30  These results 
43:886:75648:28:27:72:515:482:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:strongly support the theory that the duration of leaders affects property and contact rights in 
43:887:75744:27:28:72:244:455:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:autocracies but not in democracies. 
43:888:75779:28:27:108:542:427:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:Our theory would also predict that the time in power of "almost" autocrats -- category II in 
43:889:75871:27:28:72:522:400:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:our classification -- would matter less than the duration of less-constrained autocrats (in most 
43:890:75967:28:28:72:527:372:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:cases, the presence of a partially effective legislature is what differentiates the category I from 
43:891:76067:28:27:72:516:344:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:category II leaders).    Results from tests using Table 5 specifications, but with autocrats and 
43:892:76164:27:28:72:503:317:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:almost autocrats separated, strongly support this prediction.    For the sample of relatively 
43:893:76258:28:27:72:534:289:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:unconstrained autocrats, the AUTDUR coefficient is significant in all five cases in which it was 
43:894:76354:27:28:72:543:262:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:significant in the first panel of Table 5; in most cases the coefficient is larger in absolute value (see 
43:895:76460:28:28:72:538:234:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:Table 7).    For the relatively constrained autocrats, coefficients attain the right sign only in CIM, 
43:896:76563:28:105:72:367:206:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:BERI, and PREMIUM equations, with only CIM significant. 
43:897:76618:105:11:72:221:101:12:g_d0_f8:12:g_d0_f8:                               
43:898:76648:11:0:108:351:90:6:Times New Roman:10:Times New Roman:30  Results not shown in tables, but are available on request. 
44:899:76712:0:27:108:536:675:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:Property rights appear to deteriorate with increasing life of democratic systems (Table 5, 
44:900:76803:27:28:72:540:648:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:fourth panel).    The unexpected results here on the duration of democracy are largely the product 
44:901:76902:28:27:72:532:620:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:of a few long-lasting democracies which were replaced by reform-minded autocracies, but then 
44:902:76995:27:28:72:516:593:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:returned to democracy during our sample period.    Chile, Uruguay, and Turkey are the most 
44:903:77086:28:27:72:543:565:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:notable examples of this phenomenon.    For each of these countries, a few high DEMDUR values 
44:904:77180:27:28:72:515:538:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:are coupled with poor property rights at the outset of our sample period, and a few very low 
44:905:77273:28:28:72:533:510:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:DEMDUR values are coupled with much improved property rights at the end of the period.    In 
44:906:77366:28:27:72:507:482:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:these cases, the improvements in property rights and policies over the period are primarily 
44:907:77458:27:28:72:518:455:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:attributable to the reform-minded autocratic regimes.    These countries heavily influence the 
44:908:77553:28:27:72:537:427:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:coefficient: for DEMDUR for the sample as a whole, despite the fact that the inverse correlation 
44:909:77650:27:28:72:507:400:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:between DEMDUR and property rights measures within these countries is produced by an 
44:910:77735:28:28:72:530:372:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:interruption of democracy by autocratic rule.    Deleting these three regime-switching countries 
44:911:77832:28:27:72:522:344:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:dramatically weakens the perverse findings for DEMDUR in the CIM and BERI equations in 
44:912:77919:27:28:72:519:317:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:Table 5.    A similar weakening of those findings is obtained by using a fixed-effects test that 
44:913:78016:28:27:72:523:289:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:substitutes regime dummies for country dummies.31  The Table 5 coefficients on DEMDUR, 
44:914:78103:27:28:72:513:262:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:therefore, do not reflect an actual deterioration in property and contract rights when a given 
44:915:78197:28:28:72:225:234:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:democratic regime lasts longer. 
44:916:78228:28:28:72:75:206:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman: 
44:917:78228:28:54:72:255:178:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:6. Endogeneity of Regime Duration 
44:918:78261:54:11:72:221:124:12:g_d0_f8:12:g_d0_f8:                               
44:919:78291:11:16:108:535:113:6:Times New Roman:10:Times New Roman:31  Recall that within a democratic regime, DEMDUR always increases: DEMDUR reverts to a value of 1 
44:920:78391:16:11:72:524:97:10:Times New Roman:10:Times New Roman:only when a new democratic regime replaces a non-democratic regime.    Interruptions in democracy by spells of 
44:921:78502:11:0:72:475:86:10:Times New Roman:10:Times New Roman:autocratic rule thus cannot influence the DEMDUR coefficient when regime intercepts are included. 
45:922:78601:0:27:108:524:675:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:The time in power of autocrats is conceivably endogenous to economic performance.   
45:923:78685:27:28:72:521:648:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:Previous studies have found coup probabilities to be negatively related to recent growth rates 
45:924:78780:28:27:72:525:620:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:(Alesina et al., 1993; Londregan and Poole, 1991)32 and income levels (Londregan and Poole, 
45:925:78871:27:28:72:503:593:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:1991).    The coefficient of AUTDUR could be biased upwards if property rights improve 
45:926:78958:28:27:72:522:565:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:economic performance, which in turn improves an autocrat's survival probability and thereby 
45:927:79049:27:28:72:543:538:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:increases AUTDUR.    Another possibility is that increases in income add to autocrat duration and 
45:928:79147:28:28:72:529:510:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:improve property rights, creating a spurious association between the latter two variables.    Our 
45:929:79245:28:27:72:520:482:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:regressions control for current income levels, however.    In specifications not reported in our 
45:930:79342:27:28:72:518:455:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:tables, AUTDUR coefficients are found to be unaffected by the inclusion of growth over the 
45:931:79433:28:27:72:276:427:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:previous year as an additional regressor.33 
45:932:79476:27:28:108:539:400:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:If autocratic leaders behave in the same way as do governmental leaders in the Grossman 
45:933:79564:28:28:72:543:372:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:and Noh model, property rights could influence AUTDUR independently of the impact of property 
45:934:79657:28:27:72:522:344:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:rights on economic performance.    Though in our model higher rent extraction by an autocrat 
45:935:79750:27:28:72:534:317:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:provides more resources to maintain his hold on power, on the alternative interpretation a lower 
45:936:79847:28:27:72:543:289:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:extraction of rent from the populace would improve an autocrat's survival probability directly, and 
45:937:79947:27:28:72:391:262:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:thus generate a reverse causation from property rights to duration. 
45:938:80014:28:28:108:507:234:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:If such reverse causation were driving our results, we would expect duration in the 
45:939:80098:28:27:72:529:206:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:following period to explain current property rights better than duration in the previous period.   
45:940:80197:27:20:72:535:179:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:We introduced one-year lags and, alternatively, one-year leads of duration into our fixed-effects 
45:941:80295:20:11:72:221:159:12:g_d0_f8:12:g_d0_f8:                               
45:942:80325:11:16:108:502:148:6:Times New Roman:10:Times New Roman:32  Alesina et al. (1993) find, however, that the probability of government changes and of "major" 
45:943:80424:16:11:72:511:132:10:Times New Roman:10:Times New Roman:government changes (both of which include coups as one type of government change) is unaffected by recent 
45:944:80529:11:19:72:168:121:10:Times New Roman:10:Times New Roman:economic performance. 
45:945:80550:19:16:108:526:102:6:Times New Roman:10:Times New Roman:33  Growth in most cases is not a significant predictor of property rights.    These results are available on 
45:946:80660:16:0:72:105:86:10:Times New Roman:10:Times New Roman:request. 
46:947:80670:0:27:72:535:675:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:regressions of property rights on autocrat duration.    Neither leads nor lags performed as well as 
46:948:80770:27:28:72:513:648:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:contemporaneous duration, although differences were not dramatic.    Neither lags nor leads 
46:949:80862:28:27:72:538:620:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:clearly performed better than the other one, either.    These findings offer no support for the view 
46:950:80963:27:28:72:349:593:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:that our results are primarily capturing reverse causation. 
46:951:81022:28:27:108:543:565:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:A second piece of evidence against reverse causation is that the coefficient on AUTDUR in 
46:952:81111:27:28:72:543:538:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:most cases exceeds the coefficient on DEXDUR, the duration of democratic leaders.    A plausible 
46:953:81208:28:28:72:496:510:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:assumption is that the time in power of chief executives in democracies, as compared to 
46:954:81296:28:27:72:519:482:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:autocracies, is more sensitive to their choice of policies: indeed, this sensitivity to short-term 
46:955:81395:27:28:72:530:455:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:electoral pressures is commonly cited as a disadvantage of democracy.    Thus, the endogeneity 
46:956:81490:28:27:72:513:427:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:objection outlined above should apply as strongly, or more strongly, to the time in office of 
46:957:81584:27:28:72:533:400:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:democratic leaders.    Therefore, if reverse causation from property rights to time in power were 
46:958:81682:28:28:72:498:372:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:the primary force driving our results, coefficients for DEXDUR should exceed those for 
46:959:81769:28:27:72:500:344:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:AUTDUR.    For five of the six dependent variables in Table 5, however, coefficients for 
46:960:81858:27:28:72:509:317:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:DEXDUR and AUTDUR indicate a stronger link between duration and property rights for 
46:961:81942:28:27:72:513:289:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:autocratic leaders than for democratic leaders, as reported in more detail above.    Again, no 
46:962:82037:27:28:72:265:262:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:evidence for reverse causation is found. 
46:963:82077:28:28:108:522:234:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:Finally, we also attempted to correct for endogeneity by instrumenting for AUTDUR, 
46:964:82160:28:27:72:505:206:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:despite our skepticism concerning the appropriateness of available instruments.    The two 
46:965:82251:27:67:72:543:179:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:instruments used were age of the autocrat at the time of accession,34 and completed duration of the 
46:966:82350:67:10:72:221:112:12:g_d0_f8:12:g_d0_f8:                               
46:967:82380:10:16:108:542:102:6:Times New Roman:10:Times New Roman:34  Age is a highly imperfect measure of the time horizons relevant to policy choices by autocrats, for reasons 
46:968:82492:16:0:72:192:86:10:Times New Roman:10:Times New Roman:discussed earlier in the paper. 
47:969:82525:0:27:72:518:675:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:previous autocrat.35  As neither of these instruments varies by year, we use them only in the 
47:970:82619:27:28:72:536:648:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:country-regime regressions of property rights on AUTDUR.    Results using instrumented values 
47:971:82713:28:27:72:519:620:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:of AUTDUR were mixed.    Recall that in Table 3 AUTDUR had the predicted sign in all six 
47:972:82802:27:28:72:532:593:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:regressions.    Coefficients for instrumented values of AUTDUR are greater in absolute value in 
47:973:82898:28:27:72:543:565:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:four of these six cases, including each of the three cases (ICRG, CREDIT, and DEPREC) in which 
47:974:82993:27:28:72:542:538:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:AUTDUR was significant in Table 3.    Only in the case of DEPREC -- and of CIM, which reverses 
47:975:83087:28:28:72:539:510:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:sign -- is the instrumented value of AUTDUR statistically significant, however.    In all six cases, 
47:976:83187:28:27:72:533:482:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:standard errors are several times higher than in Table 3, due in part to reductions in sample size 
47:977:83286:27:28:72:529:455:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:attributable to missing data on the instruments, but primarily to the relatively poor explanatory 
47:978:83384:28:28:72:197:427:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:power of the instruments. 
47:979:83409:28:27:72:75:399:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman: 
47:980:83409:27:28:72:225:372:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:7. Heterogeneity of Autocrats 
47:981:83438:28:27:108:531:344:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:Our results on AUTDUR are conceivably an artifact of omitted-variable bias associated 
47:982:83524:27:28:72:539:317:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:with heterogeneity (sample selection) of autocrats.    As a simple example, suppose that autocrats 
47:983:83622:28:27:72:542:289:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:attaining power come in two types, "skilled" and "unskilled," with equal numbers in each group.   
47:984:83720:27:28:72:543:262:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:Assume further that for each group, there is a constant hazard of deposition by coup in each period, 
47:985:83821:28:28:72:531:234:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:and that this constant rate is substantially higher for the unskilled group, as depicted by the two 
47:986:83921:28:27:72:543:206:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:horizontal lines of Figure 1.    Autocrats know to which group they belong, and perceive a constant 
47:987:84021:27:32:72:542:179:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:low or high hazard rate over time, depending on whether they are skilled or unskilled.    The overall 
47:988:84123:32:11:72:221:147:12:g_d0_f8:12:g_d0_f8:                               
47:989:84153:11:16:108:542:136:6:Times New Roman:10:Times New Roman:35  Where there was no previous autocrat, as in the newly-independent African nations, we used the average 
47:990:84260:16:11:72:535:120:10:Times New Roman:10:Times New Roman:of completed duration for the initial autocrats of "similar" countries.    For example, we used the average completed 
47:991:84378:11:12:72:542:109:10:Times New Roman:10:Times New Roman:duration of all other initial autocrats in formerly-British African colonies as the instrument for AUTDUR for Uganda's 
47:992:84497:12:11:72:532:97:10:Times New Roman:10:Times New Roman:first autocrat.    Age was highly significant (t = 4.70) but previous duration only marginally significant (t = 1.64) in 
47:993:84618:11:0:72:254:86:10:Times New Roman:10:Times New Roman:explaining AUTDUR.    The R2 was only .12. 
48:994:84661:0:27:72:523:675:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:hazard rate for any given value of duration will be a weighted average of the rates for the two 
48:995:84757:27:28:72:541:648:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:separate groups.    In t = 1, the overall hazard will be exactly halfway between that for each of the 
48:996:84859:28:27:72:527:620:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:two groups, since they are represented in equal numbers at t = 1.    After that time, however, as 
48:997:84957:27:28:72:541:593:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:higher attrition in the unskilled group implies that the ratio of skilled to unskilled leaders rises, in 
48:998:85062:28:27:72:536:565:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:each subsequent year the weighted average rate of hazard will be increasingly close to the lower 
48:999:85159:27:28:72:227:538:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:hazard rate of the skilled group. 
48:1000:85192:28:28:108:535:510:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:In observing only the overall hazard rate, we attribute increasing horizons to leaders that 
48:1001:85284:28:27:72:540:482:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:survive longer in power, and hypothesize an improvement in property rights.    Yet, each autocrat 
48:1002:85382:27:28:72:543:455:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:perceives only one of the two constant hazard rates, and thus does not feel more secure in power as 
48:1003:85481:28:27:72:543:427:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:his time in power lengthens.    A consequence of heterogeneity is that it potentially makes tenure to 
48:1004:85583:27:28:72:514:400:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:date an inappropriate proxy for time horizons.    Any correlation between time in power and 
48:1005:85675:28:28:72:543:372:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:property rights may be spurious if duration has little or no relationship to the "true" time horizons 
48:1006:85777:28:27:72:186:344:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:perceived by autocrats. 
48:1007:85800:27:28:108:543:317:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:We believe the decline in hazard rates as the time in power of an autocrat lengthens is more 
48:1008:85893:28:27:72:530:289:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:than an artifact of sample selection.    First, the concept of consolidation of power is difficult to 
48:1009:85995:27:28:72:532:262:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:argue against.    Second, "skill" is only one of many factors determining who stays in power.36  
48:1010:86092:28:28:72:543:234:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:Third, some of the most important possible sources of unobserved heterogeneity may cancel each 
48:1011:86187:28:27:72:535:206:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:other out: hereditary succession may enhance a leader's legitimacy, yet his other "skills" may be 
48:1012:86285:27:28:72:510:179:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:inferior to those of a leader rising to power on his own.    Note it is not necessarily true that 
48:1013:86383:28:39:72:543:151:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:unobserved heterogeneity would bias the coefficient of AUTDUR upward.    "Charisma" may help 
48:1014:86476:39:10:72:221:112:12:g_d0_f8:12:g_d0_f8:                               
48:1015:86506:10:16:108:542:102:6:Times New Roman:10:Times New Roman:36  "Examples abound of leaders who were considered "smart" or "skilled" but who did not hold power very 
48:1016:86611:16:0:72:502:86:10:Times New Roman:10:Times New Roman:long, such as Kofi Busia in Ghana and Sylvanus Olympio in Togo." (Bienen and van de Walle, 1991, p. 6). 
49:1017:86716:0:27:72:512:675:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:a leader to stay in office, but if that charisma is based in part on an ideology antagonistic to 
49:1018:86812:27:28:72:528:648:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:markets, increases in an autocrat's time in power will be associated with deteriorating property 
49:1019:86909:28:27:72:516:620:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:rights.    In any event, we correct for this potential problem of heterogeneity, finding that the 
49:1020:87007:27:28:72:478:593:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:positive impact of autocrat duration on property rights is robust to these corrections. 
49:1021:87094:28:27:108:543:565:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:Our test is borrowed from the Abraham and Farber (1987) study of the impact of seniority 
49:1022:87183:27:28:72:507:538:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:on wages.    The long duration and favorable property-rights policies of some autocrats are 
49:1023:87275:28:28:72:515:510:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:conceivably both products of some omitted autocrat-specific characteristic, such as superior 
49:1024:87368:28:27:72:543:482:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:"skills."    In principle, we could include autocrat dummies in our fixed effects tests.    Collinearity 
49:1025:87473:27:28:72:447:455:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:of duration with time and income made these very demanding tests, however. 
49:1026:87547:28:27:108:518:427:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:Abraham and Farber faced a similar problem in attempting to control for unobserved 
49:1027:87630:27:28:72:516:400:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:worker skills and worker-job "match" in time-series cross-sectional regressions of wages on 
49:1028:87722:28:28:72:509:372:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:seniority and experience.    They could not estimate job-specific effects because changes in 
49:1029:87815:28:27:72:543:344:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:seniority and experience over time were perfectly collinear within a given job.    As an alternative, 
49:1030:87917:27:28:72:534:317:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:they included as an additional regressor completed job duration, as a proxy of these unobserved 
49:1031:88013:28:27:72:146:289:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:characteristics. 
49:1032:88029:27:28:108:531:262:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:Analogously, we include terminal duration in a time-series cross-section model without 
49:1033:88116:28:28:72:537:234:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:country- or autocrat-specific intercepts.    For each country-year observation, TERMDUR equals 
49:1034:88210:28:27:72:528:206:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:the (log of) duration of the autocrat in his final year in power.    Unmeasured skills of autocrats 
49:1035:88310:27:28:72:439:179:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:formerly captured by AUTDUR are hence captured by TERMDUR instead. 
49:1036:88376:28:28:108:528:151:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:The addition of TERMDUR has relatively little effect on the results for AUTDUR (see 
49:1037:88460:28:27:72:519:123:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:Table 8, where column 1 equations do not contain TERMDUR but column 2 equations do).   
49:1038:88547:27:0:72:527:96:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:TERMDUR has the positive sign implied by the sample selection objection in only four of six 
50:1039:88641:0:27:72:528:675:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:cases and is never significant.    AUTDUR retains the expected sign in five of six cases (all but 
50:1040:88739:27:28:72:543:648:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:ICRG), with the coefficient rising substantially in two cases (CIM and BERI).    Property rights are 
50:1041:88840:28:27:72:537:620:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:generally found to improve with autocrat duration, independently of autocrat skills, as measured 
50:1042:88937:27:28:72:244:593:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:by differences in terminal duration. 
50:1043:88973:28:28:72:75:565:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman: 
50:1044:88973:28:27:72:232:537:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:8. Additional Robustness Tests 
50:1045:89003:27:28:108:526:510:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:The ranges of several of the dependent variables -- both objective and subjective -- are 
50:1046:89090:28:27:72:529:482:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:limited.    Most notably, CIM is bounded by 0 and 1, while CREDIT is bounded by 0 and 100.   
50:1047:89182:27:28:72:538:455:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:Using OLS on these variables could lead to predicted values outside these bounds.    In fact, very 
50:1048:89281:28:27:72:542:427:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:few predicted values violated these bounds.    Re-estimating all CIM and CREDIT equations using 
50:1049:89377:27:28:72:541:400:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:logistic transformations of CIM and of CREDIT/100, constraining the predicted values to the 0-1 
50:1050:89473:28:28:72:395:372:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:interval, yielded results very similar to those reported in the tables. 
50:1051:89544:28:27:108:510:344:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:Each fixed-effects regression was re-run using corrections for autocorrelation.    All 
50:1052:89631:27:28:72:544:317:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:duration effects that were statistically significant in the tables reported here remained significant.   
50:1053:89736:28:27:72:495:289:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:Random-effects specifications were also run.    In these tests, duration of autocrat leader 
50:1054:89828:27:28:72:521:262:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:significantly improved values on all six dependent variables; AUTDUR was not a significant 
50:1055:89918:28:28:72:499:234:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:predictor of CREDIT in the fixed-effects results of Table 5.    A Hausman test rejects the 
50:1056:90009:28:27:72:461:206:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:random-effects specification in favor of the fixed-effects specification, however. 
50:1057:90091:27:28:108:543:179:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:The country-regime units cover widely-varying periods: some last less than one year while 
50:1058:90180:28:28:72:542:151:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:others cover 30 or more years.    Accordingly, we re-ran all country-regime tests reported in Tables 
50:1059:90281:28:27:72:526:123:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:1 and 3 weighting observations by the (square root of) duration of the regime.    Results on the 
50:1060:90378:27:0:72:543:96:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:regime type and duration variables vary somewhat from OLS, but not in a consistent direction, and 
51:1061:90478:0:27:72:524:675:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:lead to similar conclusions.    Furthermore, the error variance of the unweighted regressions is 
51:1062:90575:27:28:72:543:648:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:generally uncorrelated with regime duration.    We therefore report OLS rather than WLS results in 
51:1063:90674:28:27:72:447:620:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:our tables.    All standard errors reported in tables are White-corrected (1980). 
51:1064:90755:27:28:72:75:593:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman: 
51:1065:90755:28:27:72:149:565:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:9. Conclusions
