51:1066:90769:27:28:108:506:538:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:We began with a theory of the incentives and constraints that explain property and 
51:1067:90852:28:28:72:539:510:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:contracts rights in autocracies and in democracies.    We argued that a secure autocrat with a long 
51:1068:90952:28:27:72:527:482:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:time horizon has an incentive to respect and protect property and contract rights in his domain 
51:1069:91048:27:28:72:519:455:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:because this increases the future income of his domain and thus also his tax collections.    By 
51:1070:91144:28:27:72:507:427:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:contrast, an autocrat who, because of an insecure hold on power or any other reason, has a 
51:1071:91235:27:28:72:517:400:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:sufficiently short time horizon will find that the tax yield from any asset over that short time 
51:1072:91332:28:28:72:500:372:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:horizon is less than the value of the capital good, so that he is rational to seize any easily 
51:1073:91427:28:27:72:163:344:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:confiscable assets. 
51:1074:91446:27:28:108:543:317:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:In democracies, we argued, property and contract rights arise from a dramatically different 
51:1075:91538:28:27:72:537:289:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:set of incentives and constraints.    There is no reason why the election that initiates a democracy 
51:1076:91639:27:28:72:518:262:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:should bring good property and contract rights.    Democracies often emerge in unsettled and 
51:1077:91732:28:28:72:537:234:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:sometimes even somewhat anarchic conditions that are unfavorable to the protection of property 
51:1078:91827:28:27:72:526:206:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:rights and the new democracies may not be strong enough to protect these rights.    Even if the 
51:1079:91923:27:28:72:533:179:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:leadership of the new elected government is powerful, there is no assurance that property rights 
51:1080:92020:28:28:72:511:151:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:will be secure, for this democratic government may not last long, and one of the prominent 
51:1081:92111:28:27:72:438:123:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:possibilities is that the democratically elected leader will become a dictator. 
51:1082:92190:27:0:108:537:96:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:By contrast, it is not feasible for a long-lasting democracy to prohibit all forms of private 
52:1083:92286:0:27:72:525:675:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:property and contracting: the same adherence to the rule-of-law and protections for individual 
52:1084:92381:27:28:72:542:648:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:freedoms that are needed to maintain free elections in which any defeated incumbents step down, 
52:1085:92477:28:27:72:518:620:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:entail that there are some property rights -- the individuals in a free society have what James 
52:1086:92572:27:28:72:542:593:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:Madison called "a property in their rights."    Thus we hypothesized that long-lasting democracies 
52:1087:92671:28:27:72:499:565:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:generally provide better property and contract rights than either transient democracies or 
52:1088:92762:27:28:72:132:538:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:autocracies. 
52:1089:92774:28:26:108:540:510:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:Our empirical evidence supports our hypotheses.    We found that autocrats who had been 
52:1090:92862:26:27:72:543:484:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:in power longer and who by our argument had reason to have longer time horizons were associated 
52:1091:92958:27:26:72:545:457:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:with better property and contract rights than autocrats who were in power only for a shorter time.   
52:1092:93058:26:26:72:536:431:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:We also found that, in general, democracies provide greater security of property and contractual 
52:1093:93155:26:26:72:543:405:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:rights than autocracies.    But these benefits of democracy did not appear quickly: the property and 
52:1094:93255:26:26:72:521:379:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:contract rights were often poor in democracies that had lasted only a short time.    Among the 
52:1095:93350:26:26:72:543:353:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:relatively small group of countries within our sample that moved from one regime type to another, 
52:1096:93448:26:26:72:542:327:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:the security of property and contract rights was greater while they were autocracies than while they 
52:1097:93548:26:27:72:535:301:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:were democracies.    We found, by contrast, that long-lasting democracies offer better protection 
52:1098:93646:27:26:72:435:274:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:for property and contract rights than any other regime type of any duration. 
52:1099:93722:26:26:108:525:248:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:Our results also show that, as our theory predicted, the duration of democratic systems 
52:1100:93809:26:26:72:519:222:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:matters much more than the duration of democratic leaders for property and contract rights.   
52:1101:93902:26:26:72:529:196:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:Moreover, we found that, after controlling for country effects, the security of property rights is 
52:1102:94001:26:26:72:532:170:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:more sensitive to changes in the time in power of autocratic leaders than to the time in office of 
52:1103:94100:26:27:72:168:144:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:democratic leaders. 
52:1104:94119:27:26:108:501:117:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:We conclude that statistical tests of economic performance under autocracies and 
52:1105:94200:26:0:72:542:91:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:democracies that leave out the hypotheses that we have developed and tested are mis-specified.    It 
53:1106:94303:0:26:72:519:675:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:is only natural, given our theory and our empirical results, that the comparisons of economic 
53:1107:94397:26:26:72:539:649:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:performance under autocracies and democracies have been so varied and inconclusive.    It is, we 
53:1108:94494:26:26:72:524:623:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:argue, just as important in the analysis of government and politics as in the analysis of market 
53:1109:94590:26:26:72:527:597:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:behavior to analyze the incentives and constraints that face the individuals involved.    Such an 
53:1110:94688:26:26:72:527:571:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:analysis suggests that property and contract rights in democracies and autocracies have utterly 
53:1111:94784:26:0:72:385:545:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:different sources, and our empirical results show that this is true. 
54:1112:94854:0:13:72:332:675:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman: Appendix 
54:1113:94862:13:14:72:387:662:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman: The Gurr-Banks Annual Scheme

54:1120:95088:14:14:72:539:565:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:1. Selection of chief exec. [hereditary succession, or rigged elections, or by coups, or by military 
54:1121:95189:14:13:72:360:551:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:designation, or repeated incumbent selection of successors] 
54:1122:95248:13:14:72:534:538:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:2. Dual/transitional [Dual means there are two executives, one chosen by hereditary succession,

54:1138:95954:14:14:72:397:317:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:outweighs but does not completely dominate that of the legislature.
